Reopening of Naval Talks Due to Simon's Diplomatic Efforts

Britain to Propose New Plan to Break Deadlock

Anglo-Japanese Consultations Held Four Times Yesterday

[London] It is generally believed that today's naval talks will be of a critical nature. British chief representative Foreign Secretary Simon will propose a method to bring the American representative into the proceedings, so that the talks can be restarted on a tripartite basis. The British and Japanese representatives are currently engaged in busy consultations, while the American representative has no scheduled meetings, but eagerly awaits the results of the Anglo-Japanese meeting. The American representative believes that the outcome of this meeting will be of great importance to the overall situation of the talks' future. It is expected that the second step will be a meeting between the British and American representatives tomorrow.

The British and Japanese representatives continued naval talks in the House of Commons from 4:00 PM today, lasting at least an hour. Atherton of the American delegation held confidential discussions on naval talks at the British Foreign Office this morning. (Reuters, 7th)

[London] In the naval talks, the Japanese delegation has opposed all proposals that do not include Japan achieving equal rights. Therefore, the British side seems to want to propose a new compromise plan that is more easily acceptable to the Japanese side. The British delegation intends to follow the proposal made by the Japanese Ambassador to the United States, Saito (who was previously stationed in Washington), to grant Japan the right to naval parity gradually. If the Japanese government representatives reject this plan in its entirety, or reject the manner of its implementation, then the British delegation intends to make further concessions. It is heard that Britain is considering a method to abolish the quantitative limitations on naval strength but still maintain qualitative limitations. In other words, the three major naval powers, Britain, the United States, and Japan, can freely build all types of warships without any restrictions on their number, but the tonnage of each type of warship and the size of its gun caliber must comply with strict limitations. This afternoon, the entire British delegation will meet with the Japanese delegation. It is expected that at least the aforementioned British proposal will be presented at today's meeting. (Havas, 7th)

Anglo-American Representatives' Meeting Opens Door for Japan

U.S. Expresses Willingness to Continue Talks on a New Basis

Persuading Japan to Comply

[London] Following diplomatic efforts by Britain, the representatives of Britain, the United States, and Japan will continue their talks in full this week. This afternoon, British Foreign Secretary Simon received the chief American representative, Davis, at the Foreign Office for a meeting lasting one hour and fifteen minutes. The two mainly studied the current situation from the perspectives of Britain and the United States. Simon proposed a plan to continue the talks and earnestly stated that the British government wished to see all parties reach an understanding, so that the 1935 conference could be convened and have some hope of success. Davis stated that the American delegation did not want to end this meeting without studying all possible opinions. The American delegation was willing to listen to everything the Japanese government wanted to propose. At the same time, he believed that procedural issues were very difficult if they wanted to maintain the existence of the London discussions. Davis also told Simon that the American delegation was prepared to continue talks on a new basis in line with Simon's intentions. After Davis made this assurance, the news was announced that the delegations of the three countries would resume talks in full this week, preceded by a meeting of the British and Japanese delegations. (Reuters, 6th)

Britain Seeks Mediation to Save Stalemate

To Suggest Slightly Revised Ratio

American and Japanese Views Remain Divergent

[London] It is generally expected that the preliminary naval talks will reopen, and it is believed that the British side will seek a way to mediate between Japan and the United States. This impression arose after Foreign Secretary Simon met with American representative Davis this afternoon. If Japan's approval is obtained, a meeting of Britain, Japan, and the United States may be convened tomorrow. However, the reopening of preliminary talks should not be regarded as progress in the situation, nor should it be seen as a convergence of opinions. The United States and Japan still insist on their own positions. It is unknown on what basis the talks will be reopened. According to British political circles, the British delegation will only reiterate the conciliatory suggestions it has already made at the next meeting, and advocate seeking a compromise between the current 5:5:3 ratio and the naval parity demanded by Japan. In other words, adopting a ratio close to 5:5:4. This approach is simply a renewed effort on a basis that is already known to everyone. The suggestion of a 5:5:4 ratio is not new. However, this ratio is not welcomed by either the United States or Japan. As for the abolition of the Washington Treaty, what the British and American delegations emphasize is to ascertain the date on which Japan declares the abolition, and not to prevent it. The facts discovered yesterday by the League of Nations Mandates Commission from reviewing the report on Japan's rule over the Pacific Islands show that Japan has already violated the League of Nations Covenant in fact. (According to Article 22 of the League of Nations Covenant, no military installations may be set up in mandated territories). However, general opinion believes that Japan will formally declare the abolition of the Washington Treaty before the League of Nations discusses the issue of Japan's violation of the League of Nations Covenant in the Pacific Islands. (Havas, 6th)

London Times Elaborates on Naval Situation

Breakdown of Negotiations Invites Competition

Little Possibility of Conflict Between Britain and the United States

[London] As the preliminary naval talks are about to reopen, the Times published an editorial stating that the Washington Naval Treaty has become obsolete and that a new treaty limiting navies must be found to replace it. It said, "The purpose of the naval talks here is to lay the foundation for next year's naval conference, so that there is a possibility of establishing a new agreement. Even if only the ground can be leveled at this time, so that construction can begin in the future, the world will not necessarily be harmed. As far as Britain is concerned, its only main point of view is that even if the naval talks break down, the impact will be that the United States' existing shipbuilding plan, which is already very large, will be further expanded. Britain will not be alarmed by this and will deal with it calmly, because there is absolutely no possibility of conflict between the British and American navies. Even at the end of the world's civilization, they will not think of resorting to arms. Furthermore, the situation between Britain and the United States is indeed such that the British Empire's self-governing dominions such as Canada and Australia are all located on the Pacific coast. Their concern for maintaining the balance of power in the Pacific and for a satisfactory resolution of the naval issue may even surpass that of the mother country. It goes without saying that there is even less possibility of conflict between them and the increasingly large navy of the United States. All of this is indeed the real situation. But if it is said that Britain and the United States are about to form or are willing to form a united front to deal with Japan, then this is absolutely not the truth. Britain's sympathetic feelings and friendly relations with Japan have been long-standing and have not changed to this day, and Japan's desire not to be in an inferior position is also deeply understood by British people. However, naval competition is enough to lead to bankruptcy, and in Japan, its impact is even worse. Therefore, the three largest naval powers, Britain, Japan, and the United States, must work together to avoid it. In any case, qualitative restrictions must ultimately be maintained. In other words, competition regarding the tonnage of warships and the size of their guns can be avoided. Otherwise, if any country wants to build a larger navy and heavier warships, the result will inevitably be the total bankruptcy of its finances, and how can it be taken lightly? Moreover, the Washington Treaty contains important provisions regarding the construction of defensive fortifications by various countries in the Pacific islands and their policies towards China. The principles on which it is based are 'security equality' and 'China's territorial integrity.' These are the principles that cannot be abandoned in the current talks. Now, if we are good at overturning these principles before finding suitable replacements, the responsibility is so great that no one can bear it." (Havas, 7th)

Death Ray Gun Successfully Tested

Intense Beam Causes Intoxication

Power Can Cause Aircraft to Lose Control

New Invention by French Engineer

[Paris] The inventor of the death ray gun told the Associated Press that several countries are now competing to purchase the manufacturing secrets of the death ray gun. The light can cause aviators to crash to the ground. French engineer Jacques Cremas said, "This invention has now moved beyond the experimental stage. Our experiments, initially with a reduced model shaped like a rifle, have now successfully launched the death ray. The French military authorities are now helping us expand this principle and are using special equipment in the fortresses of Cherbourg, Toulon, and L'Île d'Yeu for our application. Although foreign representatives have negotiated with us repeatedly, we are unwilling to sell without the permission of the French government." Cremas continued, "He, his brother, and an Austrian engineer named Reil Hoescher, completed today's invention after two years of experimentation. The death ray gun does not kill, but it only temporarily causes people to lose consciousness. People who are hit by the death ray are as if they are drunk. It only causes aviators to lose the ability to control their aircraft. The light is taken from a type of gold material produced in the United States or Germany. The light emitted by this metal is extremely strong, several times stronger than the light emitted by manganese. This light can be extended to eight or twelve seconds without dissipating. If you want to extend it further, it is not allowed by the facts, because the high heat is enough to melt the barrel of the gun." (National News Agency, 7th)

Grand Celebrations of the October Revolution in the Soviet Union

Three-Day National Holiday

[Moscow] The Moscow Soviet held a grand meeting at the Bolshoi Theatre tonight to celebrate the 17th anniversary of the October Revolution. The central organs of the Communist Party, the Soviet government, and trade unions all participated in the meeting. Stalin, Molotov, Voroshilov, Kaganovich, Kalinin, and members of the Central Committee of the Communist Party and the government sat on the stage. A speech was delivered by Kalinin, Chairman of the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union.

The Soviet Union is celebrating the 17th anniversary of the October Revolution with a three-day holiday, which began today. The capital has taken on a joyous festive appearance, with decorations, models, charts, and drawings everywhere, showing the development of various departments in the Soviet Union over the past 17 years. At the same time, the reconstruction and improvement work of Moscow's architecture has just been completed. Some old buildings that hindered traffic have been demolished, replaced by wide streets and large squares. Tall buildings have removed their scaffolding overnight, changing the face of Moscow. The decoration of streets and squares shows the various stages of development of the Soviet Union, and there are models of the first section of the Moscow subway, which has now been completed, and the Moscow-Volga Canal, which is currently being dredged. Workers and collective farmers from all over the country have sent representatives to participate in the celebrations, and a large number of foreign workers' delegations have gathered here.

The newspapers detail the achievements of the Soviet Union in politics, culture, and economics. Izvestia said, "The foundation of socialism has been extremely firm and solid, and no counter-revolutionary sewage can shake it, and no imperialist cannon can destroy it, because our country has been completely transformed. At the same time, in the large-scale factories, collective farms, mechanized mines, and even airplanes, submarines, Arctic stations, and the fearless navy, our newly rising people are guarding them at all times. These people have been deeply trained, and they will definitely fight against their class enemies and their blind natural forces. The working masses are opening up a new record in human history, obtaining their true, not illusory, freedom, working and creating for their own benefit, and gradually producing the material conditions to achieve thorough and universal happiness. This struggle is extremely arduous, but no force in the world can stop its progress, because the laws of human development have stipulated the inevitable universal victory of the proletariat." The newspaper also commented on the Soviet Union's national defense, saying, "The world knows that the Red Army is the best army in the world today. The Red Army's armaments are the result of the high efficiency achieved by our country's industry. The excellence of the Red Army's organization is also the result of the unique organizational strength and skills of the Soviet proletariat and its party. The superiority of the military training of Red Army officers and soldiers is the result of a great cultural force, which was aroused from the Soviet workers and peasants by the October Revolution. The heroic spirit of the Red Army is also the result of the Communist Party's policy of socialist industrialization and collectivization, which has aroused the fighting spirit of Soviet workers and collective farmers. As for the unity of Red Army soldiers, it is also a product of the proletariat dictatorship crushing all domestic class enemies." The newspaper continued, "The failure of the disarmament conference and the arms race currently underway both indicate that a new world imperialist war is imminent. Fascist adventurers are trying to direct the tide of war towards the Soviet Union, but their hope of forming an anti-Soviet united front and isolating the Soviet Union has become a bubble. The internal contradictions of the imperialist powers are extremely deep, so any far-sighted person must understand this truth, that the outbreak of war, no matter where it is, will undoubtedly become a world war. As for the Soviet giant, it is always calm and vigilant in the face of the waves crashing on its shores. It already knows the greatness of its strength and can deal with and thoroughly defeat its enemies with ease. It also understands that the stronger its strength, the more friends it will gain in the struggle for peace and self-defense. It does not need war to achieve its own goals, so it implements a firm policy of peace, and at the same time, it will definitely work together with countries that do not like war to help them." (TASS, 6th)

Decision to Maintain the Truce Principle

Proposal of Compromise Methods to the Prime Minister

Almost all of those who voted in favor of the motion. The party group adjourned at more than 7:00 in the evening.

Senate Passes Motion Against Constitutional Reform Plan

[Paris] The Radical Party's attitude against the Prime Minister's reform plan and other proposals can be seen in today's Senate meeting. Senators passed a motion with 96 votes against 2, declaring that depriving the Senate of its special powers regarding the dissolution of the Chamber of Deputies is dangerous. Since the Radical Party accounts for a majority of the senators, and now opposes Doumergue's constitutional reform, a storm will inevitably be caused when the Congress is convened to approve the Prime Minister's proposal in the future. According to the Prime Minister's constitutional reform proposal, which has been approved by a majority of the cabinet, the main points are (1) limiting the number of cabinet members to 20, including the Prime Minister; (2) the President may dissolve the Chamber of Deputies in accordance with the following law: (A) within the first year of establishment, the consent of the Senate must be obtained before it can be dissolved; (B) the consent of the Senate is not required after the first year; (3) guaranteeing the positions of civil servants to avoid being forcibly dismissed. Due to the above-mentioned circumstances, more and more money is flowing into London. Air Obstacle Race between England and Australia

Australian Youth Luckily Wins Second Place Prize Money

Melbourne: The second place prize of £1,000 in this air obstacle race between England and Australia was won by Australian youth Melrose. Mr. Mears' plane arrived 14 minutes earlier than the plane driven by Stodart, so he was lucky to win the prize. Stodart submitted a protest today, saying that he lost about 24 minutes at the Alor Setar station in Malaya. Otherwise, he could have arrived earlier than Melrose, because at that time he was forced to wade through the mud to the location where the time was checked, and the staff at the Alor Setar airfield miscalculated his time to Singapore. All of this was not his fault, so the second place prize should not be given to Melrose. According to reports, Melrose was originally the third place in the obstacle race, but because Scott and Black, who won the speed race championship, could no longer receive the prize of £2,000 for the obstacle race championship, this money was given to Dutch aviators Parmentier and Moll, who won the obstacle race runner-up. Because of this, Melrose won the runner-up prize of £1,000, otherwise he would not have received a penny (Reuters, 7th).

Veteran of the French Navy, Vice Admiral Fournier, Passes Away

[Paris] Vice Admiral Fournier passed away today at the age of 92. Mr. Fournier served in China from 1865 to 1868. When the Franco-Prussian War began, Mr. Fournier returned to his country to join the army and made many achievements. In 1878, he was appointed as the commander of a gunboat and went to China again, traveling along the Bai River to Tianjin and successfully negotiating with local officials. In 1891, he was promoted to Rear Admiral and Commander of the Vietnam Fleet. Within a few years, he was promoted to Vice Admiral and appointed as the General Inspector of the Navy. He retired in 1917 due to old age and lived leisurely in the mountains and forests. Another veteran of the French Navy has passed away (Havas, 6th).

It is Hoped that the Remnant Bandits in the Border Area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui Can Be Eliminated

The Armies Encircle and Suppress in Several Routes, Leaving Only a Thousand Remnants

Zhang Xueliang Tours the Border Area of Henan and Hubei to Prepare for Relief

Hankou Communication: The remnant bandits, the false 25th and 28th armies, in the border area of the three provinces of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui have been fleeing and have not been completely wiped out for a long time. Last month, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek came to Hankou, convened military generals, and held a military conference. A new plan was decided to completely eliminate them within three months. Shangguan Yunxiang was appointed as the commander-in-chief of the pursuit and suppression, responsible for the pursuit and suppression, and the rest of the armies were responsible for intercepting. After the generals returned to their defenses, they implemented it effectively. In less than a month, the bandit forces collapsed. There were only more than 3,000 remnants left, who lacked weapons, ammunition, and food. They fled in the territory of Yingshan, Luoshan, Lihuang, and Huoshan to avoid the pursuit of the national army. On the 28th of last month, the bandits entrenched in Taojiahe, northeast of Yingshan. After Shangguan Yunxiang led his troops to suppress them, more than 500 bandits were killed in the battle of Ta'ergang. The remnant bandits fled north overnight, and were repeatedly intercepted by the Xing Liu brigades of the 11th Route Army, and were in a state of embarrassment. On the night of the 3rd of this month, the bandits fled to Hongqishan, southwest of Lihuang County, and attempted to flee west from Shuiweizi and Laofoshan. They were again caught up by the Hao detachment of the national army, and joined forces with the garrison of the 25th Route Army to attack. More than 500 bandits were killed in Shuiweizi, and the bandits' luggage and equipment, as well as the women's team and other teams, were dispersed. Only more than 1,000 remnant bandits broke through and fled to the Nanshi Luan Nihu area. Zhang Xueliang, seeing that the suppression of the bandits had been successful, took a special train on the Pinghan Railway to Huangchuan on the 1st to inspect, and convened the generals to instruct them on the opportunity to encircle and suppress in several routes, so as to eliminate them within the deadline, and at the same time prepare for the aftermath of the bandit area, and actively engage in the work of recruiting and accommodating, so as not to leave the refugees homeless. He then toured Huang'an, Macheng, Songbu, Futianhe and other places, and inspected He Zhuguo's department Niu Yuanfeng's division. He returned to Hankou on the 5th and arrived late at night. It is heard that the remnant bandits in the border area have indeed disintegrated, and it is hoped that they will be wiped out soon (6th).

After the Wuhu-Tunxi Road Opens to Traffic, Zhejiang and Anhui Passenger Cars Will Be Connected

—The Anhui Construction Department is Preparing for the Wuhu-Tunxi Road Exhibition—

Wuhu Communication: The roadbed and crushed stone pavement project of the Wuhu-Tunxi (Wuhu to Tunxi) highway in Anhui Province has now been completely completed. The entire road is more than 250 kilometers long and is handled by the Provincial Highway Bureau itself. Twenty long-distance passenger cars of Fadaer and Lihua brands were purchased. On the 1st of this month, tickets were sold in advance and passenger transport was trial-operated. The official opening ceremony will be held on New Year's Day next year. The Construction Department believes that traffic between Wuhu and Huizhou was extremely inconvenient in the past, and it was necessary to spend half a month to travel back and forth. Now, it only takes eight hours to reach directly, and the counties in Huizhou and the places along the way, such as Xuancheng, Ningguo, and Jixi, are rich in products. In order to prosper commerce and revitalize rural areas, it was decided to hold an exhibition of goods along the Wuhu-Tunxi Road on the day of the opening ceremony, so as to arouse public attention to the relationship between highways and industry, commerce, rural areas, and culture. The exhibition period is tentatively set for one month. If necessary, it can be rescheduled or extended. The exhibition is of a mobile nature and will be held in Wuhu, Xuancheng, Ningguo, Jixi, Shexian, Tunxi and other cities and towns in turn. Each place is limited to five days. The location will be borrowed from the local Chamber of Commerce or other suitable places. Preparations are now underway to actively prepare and it is expected that the future will be very effective.

The Construction Department believes that in addition to the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road, the Tunxi Highway, another transportation artery connecting southern Anhui and Zhejiang, can also directly reach Jiande Lanxi Chun'an and other counties in Zhejiang Province. Moreover, merchants in southern Anhui have long been trading with Chun'an Jian and other counties in Zhejiang Province. In the past, when the Tunxi Road was not open, passengers had to detour through Hangzhou and then follow the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, which was inconvenient in terms of both time and economy. Therefore, Wang Tiesheng was recently sent to Zhejiang to discuss the direct traffic between the two provinces. The procedures for mutual interconnection have now been identified. During the period when the two provinces are submitting for approval, the vehicles of the two provinces have been pre-connected, opening four times a day, and meeting at the provincial border in front of the Jiekou Tudimiao (6th).

Record of an Inspection in the Northwest

— Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Geng Ya

Passing Yumen and Arriving at Anxi

Traveling fifteen or sixteen li west from Chijin Fort, we crossed the Chijin River. The water came from the southern mountains, with fine sand mixed in the flow, appearing reddish-brown. We passed through the five-li Chijin Gorge, where residents lived scattered in about thirty or so households. When asked if this place produced gold, they replied that it was once said gold sand could be found in the river, but now no one dredged for it. They said that many people go to the Qilian Mountains to pan for gold every year. Afterward, we passed through the Gobi Desert, which stretched for sixty or seventy li, until we gradually saw village trees as we approached Yumen County. The city perimeter was only about three li. Entering through the south gate, above which was inscribed "Obstructing the Barbarian Hordes," we turned diagonally out of the north gate. Inside the city, the houses were closely packed, and the streets were short and narrow. There were several old poplar trees, with circumferences exceeding five chi. The walls of the houses on both sides were squeezed as if about to collapse. It is said that they were planted by Nian Gengyao during his western expedition, making them ancient relics of nearly three hundred years. The county government gate looked more like a shop front. The clothing of the men and women was not very tattered, and we did not see children without clothes. The women's figures were also quite healthy and graceful. This was due to two reasons: first, during the Tongzhi Rebellion, most of the cities in Longxi were burned to the ground, but this place was fortunately spared; second, the forests were dense, the water channels were open, and the land near the suburbs was quite fertile. The so-called essence of the Gobi finally had such a good appearance. There is an ancient poem that goes, "The Qiang flute need not resent the willow trees, for the spring breeze does not pass through Yumen Pass." (Note: The ancient Yumen Pass was still one hundred and twenty li northwest of Dunhuang.) Today, people also say, "Once you leave Jiayu Pass, even a sow looks like Diaochan." Based on current facts, these are all inaccurate poetic sayings.

A few li outside the city, we saw the Gobi Desert again, stretching for forty or fifty li, until we reached a large village called Sandaogou, which belonged to Anxi County. There were three hundred or so households, mostly Han and Hui people. There were only two or three families of "Turbaned Heads" (Uighurs) who had recently moved from Xinjiang. Shops displayed goods from Baotou and Xinjiang, and the trade was still considerable, far better than in Anxi City itself. There was a type of mineral called "Hanshui Stone," transported from Changma Mountain, which was burned with coal and suddenly turned into snow-white powder as fine as dust. It could be used to extract pigments, but the residents only used it for mending cracks and plastering walls, which was a great pity. We met two people returning from Dihua, one surnamed Zhou from Hunan, with his family of two, and one surnamed Yang from Shanhaiguan. They both said that the journey to Xinjiang was very difficult. Many of the former post stations had been demolished, and one often had to travel hundreds of li to find food and lodging. The section from Hami to Guchengzi was even more devastated by Ma Zhongying. Merchants passing through had to be cautious and travel in groups, otherwise, they would likely be attacked by Kazakhs (also a type of native Xinjiang people, similar to Turbaned Heads, but more barbaric). The Kazakhs would first lie in wait in the grass, fire a shot, and then swarm to rob and kill. The bullets they fired were not steel balls but tin pellets. They said that one pellet could hit a rabbit, and the price of the skinned rabbit was only worth two dimes. But if they used it to hit a person, no matter what, the gain would be more than the value of a rabbit skin.

After lunch, we continued westward. The water and grass along the way were lush, and the soil was loose, but the villages were sparse, and the land was wasted, which was a great pity. The only transportation route between Gansu and Xinjiang was also overgrown with grass. Only where the horses' hooves stepped and the wheels rolled left slight traces, forming a "川" (river) shape. If even this were gone, travelers would have no signs to follow and would surely get lost in the overgrown wilderness. After twenty or so li, we crossed a shallow river. The evening glow reflected beautifully, and with a sudden gust of wind, the earth was enveloped in night. Unable to reach the next station, we had to spend the night in an old temple. From Huihuibao to Yumen, the distance was fifty-one kilometers, about one hundred and fifty-three li. From Yumen to this place, the old temple near Liudaogou, the distance was twenty-one kilometers, about sixty-three li, totaling seventy-two kilometers, two hundred and sixteen li.

The old temple was surrounded by red willows (the branches and leaves were similar to junipers, but thinner, with spike-shaped red flowers, which southerners call Guanyin willows, and Westerners call beautiful). Inside were two white poplars, one with a straight trunk, rising three or four zhang, and the other with lush leaves and dense branches, spreading like an umbrella canopy, standing opposite the temple. They could be seen from dozens of li away. There was no response to our knocking. We could only glimpse the flickering Buddhist lamp in the main hall through the crack in the door. When the car first arrived, we vaguely saw someone running away, presumably the abbot of the temple, who had misunderstood and fled. At that time, the drizzle was fine, and the wind and sand were fierce, making it difficult to camp in the open. So we broke the lock and entered. The temple corridor leaked in the corners. Besides a few broken cotton wads and earthenware jars, it was empty. Pushing open the door of the main hall, we illuminated the Buddha statue with a flashlight. We first saw Zhou Cang holding a large knife, knowing it was a Guan Yu Temple. Wild pigeons nested among the beams and rafters, flapping and flying in surprise, numbering over a hundred. They then landed on the trees in the courtyard, bending the branches. The cook seized a few and was about to cook them, but then thought he might be punished by the gods, so he let them go. The next morning, we met a shepherd who said the pigeons were very old and would be difficult to swallow even if cooked. When the car manager, Mr. Tan, left, seeing that the temple master had not yet returned, he specially used a new lock to lock the temple door and gave the shepherd an empty kerosene barrel, instructing him to hand over the key to the new lock to the temple master. This shows that outsiders do not cheat people over small matters, and also leaves room to avoid being driven away on a future visit.

We traveled through the grassland in the morning, passing the Qidaogou Yao Station. In the past, it provided food and lodging, but now only ruined walls and old poplars remain, sighing in the wind. After about fifty li, we reached Bulongji City. Along the way, we saw many pools of water and lush grass, which were ideal for reclamation and animal husbandry. Occasionally, we encountered dangerous places, but there was also water and grass. Cultivating crops should be harmless. The city of Bulongji had a perimeter of about six li. During the Qing Dynasty, in the Yongzheng period, troops were stationed here to cultivate land. The Anxi garrison also established a horse farm here. There were more than ten white poplars, with tall branches shading the sun and thick shade covering the ground, about four or five armfuls in circumference, with numbered cloth signs hanging on them, reading "Planted by General Nian." The original population was seven or eight hundred households, but now only one-tenth remains. The burden on farmers and merchants has increased daily, and there are frequent reports of fleeing households, all unable to bear the exploitation of taxes. Those who do not flee are mostly impoverished. I saw small vendors selling melons, fruits, needles, and thread, setting up stalls on the spot. Women and children each held tobacco pipes, bartering for apricots. Seeing this situation, I couldn't help but feel sad for the villagers.

In the afternoon, we continued our journey. After thirty-some li, we crossed the Kulong River, which is the ancient Hulu River. There was an ancient city, the former site of the Tang Dynasty's Yumen Pass. Slightly west was Shuangtabao, the former site of the Tang Dynasty's Guazhou Jinchang County. However, there were also few residents, presenting a desolate scene. After passing the fort, we traveled uphill for about ten li. The north and south mountains stood opposite each other, with a high mound on the north mountain and twin pagodas soaring into the sky on the south mountain, a magnificent natural formation, the origin of which is unknown. The river here curved around, and the vegetation was lush. Suddenly, the mountains rose and fell, and the northern branch stretched out again. The road ran along the northern foot of the south mountain for thirty-some li, reaching Xiaowanzi, where we stayed for the night. That day, we traveled thirty-eight kilometers, about one hundred and fourteen li.

Xiaowanzi had abundant water and fertile soil, and many farmers lived there in the past. Now, due to heavy donations, many have abandoned their fields and fled. This spring, a middle-class household surnamed Wang took their family and tried to escape. The village head, fearing that it would increase the burden on those who did not flee, chased them back. Wang said he had no seeds or oxen for plowing. The village head, originally a wealthy household, generously lent them to him. They barely managed to survive until autumn, and then fled again secretly at night. They had not harvested wheat and had abandoned their furniture, catching everyone off guard, so they were not caught. The abandoned houses were complete and habitable. Although the doors were open, the earthen stoves, large jars, tables, stools, and even coffins prepared for the elderly were all intact. Only the earthen pit bed had been broken by neighbors for fertilizer. (The earthen pit bed, because people slept on it and the underside was smoked with dung grass, was replaced every year and could be used as fertilizer.) I was awakened in the middle of the night by a sudden noise. I asked and learned that Zhang Wenrui and the cook had been sleeping in a low-lying area, and the water from the canal had overflowed in the middle of the night, soaking all the bedding. Zhang and others had worked hard during the day and were snoring under their quilts until they were completely wet and cold, then they woke up and shouted in confusion, claiming that "the quilts weighed a thousand catties and they had no strength to move them." They then lit a fire to keep warm and left at dawn. After seventy li, we arrived at Anxi, and were distressed that there was no hotel to stay in. We happened to meet a friend, Fan Yuancen, who was the current head of the Anxi Special Tax Bureau, and he insisted on inviting us to stay in the bureau. The bureau was located in the Sichuan Guild Hall, which was clean, spacious, and comfortable. Finding this in the remote desert was truly fortunate.

Songjiang

Grass House Fire at Jingjia Weir

Guan Dazi, a resident of the northern shantytown in Songjiang, lived in a grass house built in Jingjia Weir with his wife, Guan Chen, and their two-year-old child. He worked as a laborer to support his family. Today (the 7th) at 4 p.m., a welcoming deity parade passed by. Spectators threw cigarette butts onto the grass house. The crowd did not pay attention. After a while, a spark ignited the entire area. Neighbors were shocked and quickly reported to the police, who relayed the message to the fire brigades in each district. They used water pumps to extinguish the fire, preventing it from spreading to neighboring houses. However, Guan Dazi, after receiving the news, was unable to rush into the grass house. Therefore, his two-year-old child was buried in the flames. Those who heard this felt deeply saddened.

Nanhui

Child Run Over and Killed by Shangnan Bus

Yesterday morning at 11 a.m., a northbound bus of the Shangnan Long-Distance Bus Company was traveling through Shenjia Bridge in Sanlintang when a child suddenly ran out from the side of the road and crossed the tracks. The driver saw this but was unable to brake in time, resulting in the child being run over and killed instantly. The child's family negotiated with the company and settled the matter with a compensation of twenty yuan.

Suzhou

Establishment of the County Land Bureau

The Wu County Land Bureau, in preparation for over a year, was officially established yesterday (the 7th). The bureau is located at the former Wu County government site on Heng Street. The director is Shen Shike. There are three sections: the General Affairs Section Chief is Zhao Tinggan, the Technical Section Chief is Pei Guanxi, and the Registration Section Chief is concurrently held by Director Shen. The Survey Team Leader is also Pei Guanxi. Staff members for each section have also been announced.

National Exhibition to Open as Scheduled

Merchants of domestic goods, led by Sun Zicheng, organized the Wu County National Goods Mobile Exhibition, scheduled to open on the 10th. However, merchants from Guanqian Street, such as Tu Haoquan and Wu Jiyuan, believed that the timing, near winter, was particularly related to the business in Guanqian Street, so they resolutely opposed it. They petitioned the County Chamber of Commerce and the County Party Headquarters, demanding that the exhibition be stopped. The County Party Headquarters, having already given permission beforehand, could not agree. Moreover, among the petitioning merchants, most also sold foreign goods, which was not in line with promoting domestic goods. The County Chamber of Commerce, wanting to please both sides, suggested only exhibiting and not moving the exhibition. However, the National Goods Mobile Exhibition did not stop due to the opposition and continued to actively prepare. Over fifty council members from domestic goods manufacturers in Shanghai arrived in Suzhou yesterday afternoon (the 7th). They were scheduled to host a banquet for the press at noon on the 8th, and to hold a meeting of factory representatives in the afternoon to select venues. On the 9th, they would invite various agencies to assess the domestic goods. The opening was still scheduled for the 10th. The opening ceremony would be held in the morning, and the mobile exhibition would begin in the afternoon. It was also rumored that the opposition might express their views in writing at the opening.

Wuxi

Reporters Association Questions Zhang Yu

Pan Kui, a reporter for the Xinmin Daily in this county, was detained by Zhang Yu, the chief of the Public Security First Sub-Bureau, for allegedly defrauding money while paying a fine on behalf of someone at the bureau. He was also subjected to illegal abuse. The case has now been transferred to the court, and Prosecutor Lian has ordered Pan Kui to be released on bail of two hundred yuan. Yesterday, the News Reporters Association of this county stated that if Pan's fraud was true, it would not only violate criminal law but also bring shame to the industry. It would be difficult to forgive him legally and ethically. They would wait quietly for the court to handle the case and first suspend his membership. However, they raised four questions regarding Zhang Yu's leading others to commit crimes and his illegal abuse: 1. The original judgment by the bureau in the case of Mo Zhongying was a fine of eight yuan, but Zhang suddenly changed it to five yuan based on Pan's words. This was either listening to solicitations or deliberately showing favoritism. Then, suddenly, he changed his attitude and treated Pan like an enemy, subjecting him to abuse outside the law. Was there any other key element in this? This is question one. 2. Listening to solicitations, exaggerating or suppressing cases, is absolutely impermissible for public officials. Now, the chief of the sub-bureau changed the judgment by selling favors. His crime is greater than soliciting tariffs. In fact, it promoted Pan's commission of a crime. Considering the chief's sudden change in attitude from respectful to disdainful, wasn't it deliberately setting a trap to induce crime? This is question two. 3. The chief of the bureau inflicted freezing torture and illegal abuse, which is not seen in our country's old or new laws. Is it recorded in the special violation penalty law made by the chief? This is question three. 4. Modern criminal law emphasizes reform, rewards repentance, prohibits abuse, encourages self-renewal, and has provisions for probation. Pan Kui's crime, in terms of sentiment, should be treated with leniency, and sending him for prosecution, in terms of fact, does not cause concern about escape. Why did you uniquely bind him with hemp rope, like a major thief, causing the audience to laugh and leaving a permanent stain? Such abuse of power to satisfy personal desires, please answer question four. We respectfully request a reply today.

Gaoyou

Fifteen Homes Robbed in Ergou Town

Ergou Town, thirty li from the city, is a prosperous commercial center. Unexpectedly, last night, seventeen or eighteen bandits, each armed with firearms, landed from a boat on the western Renzi River and extensively searched and robbed fifteen shops, including Maochang Egg Shop. After two hours, they fled with their loot, also stealing a newly built boat from the Doutian Temple in the town. The total loss was estimated to be over four thousand yuan. It was heard that Maochang Egg Shop, Yitaiyuan Grocery Store, and the Pan family suffered the greatest losses.

Qingpu

Farmers Kidnapped in Youbang Village

Last night, eight or nine bandits suddenly came to Youbang Village in the fourth district of this county. They arrived in a bandit boat, broke into the home of farmer Huang Shunfu, and bound all the family members. They ransacked the boxes and cabinets, looting everything. Before leaving, they kidnapped Huang Shunfu and his cousin, Huang Xiaoqi. When the nearby people heard the noise and tried to apprehend them, the bandits had already disappeared without a trace.

Haimen

Haimen Sojourners Association in Beijing Opposes Dredging the Tongsha River

The Haimen Sojourners Association in Beijing, concerning Chen Baochu of Nantong's proposal to dredge the Tongsha River, which runs directly through the three counties of Tonghai and Qi, telegraphed its opposition yesterday. The original telegram stated, "Recently, we read in the newspapers of this county that Chen Baochu of Nantong, in conjunction with the gentry of Tonghai and Qi counties, is proposing to dredge the Tongsha River to expedite the drainage of Nantong. If the people of our Hai and Qi counties rashly agree, it would be tantamount to turning our Hai and Qi counties into marshlands. In the second year of the Republic of China, Zhang Jian of Nantong proposed to dredge the Tongsha River in the Provincial Assembly, but the people of the county strongly opposed it, and the decision was overturned, prohibiting dredging. The iron case of the former ministry is like a mountain and cannot be moved. Now we hear that Mr. Tan Juenong (the current head of the Construction Section of the County Government), a representative of Haimen, has actually agreed with Chen's proposal, arguing that dredging the river is beneficial and harmless. Unless he is insane, how could he say this? The sojourners in Beijing, considering the location of our ancestral graves, cannot bear to sit idly by and watch the people of the two counties lament over their fish. We unanimously oppose it and ask Mr. Tan to explain in detail the benefits of dredging the river and dispel public doubts.

Special Dispatch

Implementation Report of Resolutions from the National Finance Conference

Compiled by the Local Tax and Levy Consolidation Committee of the Ministry of Finance

(I) Introduction

The efforts of various provinces and cities in abolishing excessive and miscellaneous levies, reducing local budgets, and consolidating land taxes have been reported to the nation in summaries. In recent months, progress has continued, yielding considerable results. Regarding the stamp tax collection method to compensate for revenue losses, postal offices will begin selling stamps starting in November, and inspection measures will be announced. If collection is effective in the future, tax revenue will increase, and sufficient funds will be available to compensate for the abolition of excessive levies, which should be even more significant. We now specially compile and list the key points for reference.

(I) Consolidating legitimate local taxes and levies is one of the important missions of this committee. Currently, based on the investigation of tax and levy situations in various provinces and cities, various consolidation plans are being drafted. Furthermore, the various tax and levy regulations reported by various provinces and cities are being carefully reviewed to formulate the types and scope of future local taxes and levies, aiming to eliminate all miscellaneous levies and achieve a unified tax system.

(II) Recently, most budget estimates from various provinces and cities have been submitted to the ministry in accordance with the revised budget regulations. The budget estimates of Nanjing City and Weihaiwei have been reviewed and completed by the ministry. The budget estimates of Henan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and Hunan provinces have also been submitted to the ministry successively. Various provinces are also reorganizing county-level budgets. For example, Zhejiang, Shandong, Anhui, Chahar, Suiyuan, and Guizhou provinces have drafted county budget regulations, which have been reviewed by the ministry and implemented. In the future, the handling of county and city budgets by various provinces and cities should also have a standard to follow.

(III) Regarding the land declaration case, we recently received a copy of the implementation measures forwarded by the Hubei Provincial Government. It is planned to change the original land tax consolidation plan and handle it in accordance with the guidelines issued by the Executive Yuan. The official regulations will be sent to the ministry soon. In Fujian, all counties have been notified to handle it in accordance with the guidelines issued by the Executive Yuan. Even provinces that previously requested exemption from holding such as Jiangxi Province, have now replied to the provincial government, referring to the key points and sample forms issued by the ministry, and instructed the Finance Department and Land Bureau to comply. It seems that the important policy of land declaration can now be carried out uniformly throughout the country.

(IV) According to the resolution of the National Finance Conference, each province and city should establish a Tax and Levy Supervision Committee to supervise the implementation of the abolition of excessive levies and miscellaneous taxes. It is now planned to first organize in more than ten provinces and regions, such as Jiangsu and Zhejiang. In the future, it will provide greater assistance in promoting the implementation of the National Finance Conference resolutions.

Other resolutions on important cases are also being promoted separately by various provinces and cities, with considerable achievements. They will be announced successively to satisfy the public.

(II) Reform of the Stamp Tax System

The stamp tax is one of the important compensation measures for abolishing excessive levies and reducing surcharges. The Executive Yuan has decided on a revenue-sharing method, and the Ministry of Finance has repeatedly made active plans. However, according to past performance, this tax revenue needs to be improved in many aspects, and in remote and poor areas, it may involve excessive disturbance. Therefore, when implementing revenue-sharing to local areas, the stamp sales method will be reorganized and changed to postal offices as agents to prevent the evils of contracting and apportioning. Inspection measures will be stipulated to prevent under-stamping and missing stamps. If handled properly and inspected effectively in the future, the compensation to local areas will gradually become sufficient. (Note: The Ministry of Finance's announcement and inspection measures have been reported in newspapers and are omitted here.)

(III) Revision of Budget Regulations

Local budgets are a manifestation of the local financial situation. The Ministry of Finance is responsible for supervising local finance, and it should participate in the review in advance to improve it. The National Finance Conference recognized this and made a resolution to revise the budget regulations. The ministry has recently forwarded them to the National Government for promulgation and amendment. Article 42 of the original regulations has been changed to: "Each provincial and municipal government shall, based on the annual administrative plan and the principle of balancing revenue and expenditure, discuss and determine the draft budget for the province or city and return it to the Finance Department or Finance Bureau before January 31. If the total amount of estimated expenditures exceeds the total amount of estimated revenues, the provincial or municipal government shall discuss and determine remedial measures and submit them to the central government for approval." Article 43 has been changed to: "Each provincial Finance Department or municipal Finance Bureau shall, based on the annual administrative plan and draft budget discussed and determined by the provincial or municipal government, compile the total estimated revenue and expenditure for the province or city (i.e., the second-level budget) and submit five copies, along with the annual administrative plan, before February 15. One copy shall be sent to the Executive Yuan, one to the Ministry of Finance, and three copies, along with one copy of the first-level budget each, to the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government. After receiving the second-level budget and administrative plan from each province and city, the Executive Yuan shall immediately convene a review meeting of the relevant ministries and commissions, prepare a written review opinion, and submit it to the Executive Yuan meeting for approval before March 15, and forward it to the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government." Article 44 has been changed to: "The Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government shall review the total estimated revenue and expenditure of each province and city, sign and comment on it, and submit two copies of the total estimated budget, along with one copy each of the review opinions of the Executive Yuan and the Directorate-General of Budget, before March 31, to the Central Political Council through the National Government." After this, local budgets can gradually enter the right track.

(IV) Summary of Provincial Reports

Jiangxi Province: The Ministry received a letter from the Jiangxi Provincial Finance Department reporting that the province's consolidation of county-level finance is based on unified revenue and expenditure and determined budgets as a starting point. All revenue and expenditure of each county is managed by the County Finance Committee and submitted to the Provincial Affairs Conference for discussion and resolution. All members of the committee and the director of the Security Department organize the County Local Budget Review Committee. All county budgets are compiled by each county and sent to the department, which conducts a preliminary review. For revenue, land tax surcharges are reduced, and excessive and miscellaneous taxes and levies are eliminated. For expenditure, redundant institutions are merged, redundant personnel are reduced, and all unnecessary or avoidable extravagant expenditures are eliminated. Unified collection and expenditure must be appropriate, and then submitted to the Provincial Government Local Budget Review Committee for review to ensure accuracy and detail. Once passed and decided, it will be forwarded to the provincial government for promulgation and compliance. The budgets of all counties in the province have now been submitted for approval, and according to another case report, the reduction of land tax surcharges is estimated to be more than 3 million, and the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes and levies is estimated to be more than 1 million.

Fujian Province: The Ministry continued to receive a letter from the Fujian Provincial Finance Department reporting that the province initially planned to implement county-level budgets after the establishment of finance bureaus. However, due to the intrusion of Red bandits in various places, it is temporarily difficult to abolish the group fee surcharge, and the responsibility of the county magistrate to collect taxes has not been clearly defined for the time being. Therefore, it is temporarily difficult to start county-level budgets. It is planned to wait until the situation is slightly stable, and first summon and train the financial personnel in the county as preparation for future budget compilation and review. In addition, ten implementation plans for consolidating land tax, four plans for consolidating deed tax, three implementation plans for consolidating slaughter tax, nine implementation plans for consolidating house and shop tax, four implementation plans for consolidating business tax, and seven notes for collecting business tax should be formulated and issued to various collection agencies for earnest implementation.

Hubei Province: The Ministry continued to receive a letter from the Hubei Provincial Finance Department reporting that the first batch of 27 types of commercial port levies, totaling 286,000 yuan, have been abolished, as detailed in the previous report. The county-level revenue and expenditure budgets for the 23rd year of each county have now been reviewed, approved, and implemented. In summary, the reduction of land tax surcharges includes 21 counties such as Wuchang, totaling 520,220 yuan. The abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes and levies includes 39 counties such as Puqi, with 62 tax items, totaling 451,948 yuan. The Wuxue commercial port continues to abolish two types of levies, the salt merchant donation and the pier tax, totaling approximately 250 yuan. The total reduction of the three items is 972,419 yuan. As for land tax surcharges exceeding the regular tax, due to the need for funds, it was temporarily impossible to reduce them. Excessive and miscellaneous taxes and levies related to education expenses that cannot be abolished temporarily before funding is obtained have been reduced in accordance with central regulations within a limited time and supervised to be reduced separately within the time limit. On the one hand, the county will formulate alternative compensation measures and submit them for approval and compliance. The rest are strictly reduced in the current year's budget of each county in order to implement the central government's purpose of reducing the people's suffering.

Suiyuan Province: The Ministry approved the telegram from Fu Zuoyi, Chairman of the Suiyuan Provincial Government, stating that Suiyuan Province is located in a remote area, and the people are struggling. This year, it is planned to exempt all arrears of taxes and levies for the 17th and 18th years, totaling more than 390,000 yuan. It is also planned to merge the four bureaus of each county into departments and continue to reduce redundant institutions, saving 340,000 yuan annually. The security regiments will gradually achieve a non-paid system, and the first year is planned to reduce a part of it, saving more than 100,000 yuan annually. For village apportionments, the county is ordered to earnestly supervise and eliminate the harassment of urging and demanding from the village officials. Village regiments rotate services without paying salaries, reducing recurring expenditures. By proceeding in this way, the burden on the people of Suiyuan can be reduced by at least 700,000 yuan this year. Regarding the original taxes and levies in Suiyuan Province that should be abolished, they include 13 items: Koubei Mongolian Salt, Food Household Donation, Kuai Donation, Coal Tax, Freight Tax, Oil Tax, Wugongba Road Construction Donation, Pig Bristle Donation, Public Debt Surcharge Charcoal Juice Donation, Boat and Raft Escort Fee, Office Fee Attached to Boat and Raft Escort, Jiancao Boat License Fee, and Nursery Expenses, totaling a reduction of more than 200,000 yuan in annual revenue. Except for the Wugongba Road Construction Donation, which was abolished on August 1, the rest are planned to be handled in two phases. Starting from October 1, the Nursery Expenses, Koubei Mongolian Salt Food Household Donation, Public Debt Surcharge Dou Donation, Pig Bristle Donation, and Oil Tax will be abolished. The rest will be handled on a scheduled basis. As for the donations and fees that should be abolished at the county level, the categories are numerous and closely related to the people's pain. The department is ordering the county bureaus to investigate and then separately verify the retention and abolition.

Shaanxi Province: The Ministry received a letter from the Shaanxi Finance Commissioner stating that the Shaanxi Province should implement the abolition of excessive levies as resolved by the National Finance Conference in order to reduce the burden on the people. The total amount of taxes and levies abolished in Shaanxi Province before and after has reached more than 100,000 yuan. According to a telegram from the Finance Department, the abolition of excessive levies in Shaanxi Province reflects the central government's virtue and embodies the determination to implement it. It is now planned to first abolish 61 types of county-level taxes and levies, totaling more than 280,000 yuan. An administrative conference of various county magistrates has been convened to discuss implementation plans for consolidating land tax and levies and to proceed earnestly.

Chahar Province: The Ministry continued to receive a letter from the Chahar Provincial Finance Department stating that Chahar Province had abolished 25 types of miscellaneous levies in various counties, totaling 20,870 yuan in foreign currency, between May and June of this year. The number of apportionments cancelled in various counties reached 511,779 yuan. It is also proposed to implement the abolition of corvee in various counties starting from January 1, 24th year, totaling 11,186 yuan in foreign currency, 91,187 yuan in land tax surcharges, and 219,000 yuan in provincial local donations.

Jiangsu Province: The Ministry continued to approve the report from the Jiangsu Provincial Government stating that local miscellaneous levies in various counties in Jiangsu have been reorganized by sending personnel. The first and second batches of excessive and minor levies have been abolished separately. All levies that should be abolished in the third batch have now been reorganized, totaling 88 types, with a total of 95,521 yuan in silver annually. The Finance Department has ordered the relevant counties to implement the abolition. In addition, various miscellaneous levies are still being actively reorganized.

Hunan Province: The Hunan Provincial Finance Department recently reported on the situation of reducing land tax surcharges, stating that it is planned to reduce the group fee surcharge by 80% per tael, reducing more than 940,000 yuan annually. As for the various surcharges that still exceed the regular tax, it is planned to reduce them in three years, reducing one-third each year. For counties that have requested the collection of surcharges for a certain project, if the project has been completed or terminated, they will be ordered to abolish it immediately. The temporary mu tax apportionment in various counties and towns has also been strictly prohibited. Those that have been reduced now include Liling, Cili, Rucheng, Xinhua, Dayong, Qiyang, Chen County, Hengshan, and other counties, calculated according to the assessed amount, totaling approximately 390,000 yuan.

Guizhou Province: The Ministry received a report from the Guizhou Provincial Finance Department stating that Guizhou Province is poor and the counties collect complex and varied levies. Since receiving the order to abolish excessive levies, it has been divided into three phases, with two months as one phase, ending at the end of December of the 13th year. The excessive and miscellaneous levies abolished in the first phase totaled more than 16,000 yuan. It is still actively proceeding to ensure that all excessive and miscellaneous taxes and levies in the counties of Guizhou Province are abolished before the end of December of the 23rd year in order to relieve the people's distress and comply with the law.

Holiday on the 12th, All Sectors to Celebrate by Displaying Flags

Banking Sector Discussed Loan to Shaanxi Province for Wei River Diversion Yesterday

Total Amount of 1.5 Million Yuan

Guaranteed by Jing and Luo Water Conservancy Donations

According to the Central News Agency, the Shaanxi Provincial Government is actively carrying out water conservancy construction throughout the province. Since the completion of the Jinghui and Luohui canals, farmland irrigation has been convenient. It is now planned to divert the Wei River to irrigate farmland and build the Weihui Canal. The required funds are 1.5 million yuan. After Yang Hucheng, the Pacification Director stationed in Shaanxi, came to Shanghai last time to negotiate a loan with the banking sector, the principles have been determined. The provincial government has sent Lei Baohua, Director of the Construction Department, to Shanghai to negotiate again. A contract will be signed soon. According to the reporter's inquiry, the details are as follows:

Loan for Wei River Diversion

Shaanxi Province has suffered from drought for many years, and farmland has been abandoned. In order to actively promote construction, the provincial authorities have jointly formulated detailed plans with the National Economic Council to gradually improve water conservancy. The Jinghui and Luohui canals have been completed, and farmland irrigation has benefited greatly. It is now planned to guide the Wei River to build a gate, which is scheduled to be completed in the summer of the 25th year. The canal is 200 li long and can irrigate more than 7,000 hectares of farmland. The magnitude of the project and its relationship to farmers can be imagined.

Principles Determined

The provincial authorities are eager to proceed with the project, so Yang Hucheng once borrowed 1.5 million yuan from the bank in Shanghai, guaranteed by the Jing and Luo canals' water donations. The banking sector has agreed to the principles of the loan, but the use of water donations as a guarantee is still to be negotiated. Lei Baohua, Director of the Construction Department of Shaanxi Province, came to Shanghai and learned of this situation. He immediately telegraphed the province to send the water donation measures and the organizational rules and regulations of the collection agencies to Shanghai for the banking sector to study. It was sent yesterday.

Discussion of Measures

The banks then met at 11:00 AM yesterday at the third floor of the Central Bank to discuss the loan. Chen Xing of the Central Bank, Liu Tao of the Bank of China, Jin Guobao and Zhang Peishen of the Bank of Communications, Chen Liting of the Jincheng Bank, Chen Guangfu and Cheng Muhai of the Shanghai Bank, and others attended. Director Lei also attended the meeting and reported, and submitted the draft contract he brought to the representatives for discussion. After some modifications, it was handed over to the Central Bank to draft separately. At noon, Zhang Gongquan, General Manager of the Bank of China, hosted a banquet for the representatives of the six banks at the Bank Club to continue the discussion.

Contract Content

As for the contract content, according to the reporter's inquiry, the total loan amount is 1.5 million yuan, which will be underwritten by six banks including the Central Bank. However, the number of loans to be borne by each bank has not yet been determined. The loan period is from the end of the 25th year and will be repaid in installments until the end of the 28th year. The guarantee is the water donation from the Jinghui and Luohui canals. A Water Donation Supervision Committee will be organized with representatives from the bank to demonstrate credit. The loan interest rate has not yet been determined and will be discussed further. However, since the bank has no objection to the collateral and the contract is being drafted, the formal signing should not be far away.

Lei Baohua, Director of the Shaanxi Construction Department, Talks About Shaanxi's Efforts in Construction

People from the Southeast Eager to Invest and Development is Promising

Highways, Municipal Administration, Water Conservancy, and Electricity are Gradually Being Implemented

According to the Central News Agency, Lei Baohua, Director of the Construction Department of Shaanxi Province, has been in Shanghai for several days to negotiate a loan for the Wei River diversion. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mr. Lei at his residence. According to his conversation, various constructions in Shaanxi Province are being actively carried out. The Chinese people are now paying close attention to the construction in the Northwest and are working hard to assist. If it can proceed in an orderly manner, the future is very promising. The following is a transcript of his conversation:

Development is Promising

Director Lei first said that he had only been in Shaanxi for five months. Various constructions, such as the important highways in the province and the municipal administration of Xi'an, are all under the direction of the government and are being carried out diligently. People from all over the country, especially those from the southeastern provinces, have paid close attention to the construction in the Northwest in recent years and have benefited greatly from investing and developing there. This year, the province has had a bumper harvest, and the rural situation is better. We should focus on the priorities and proceed in an orderly manner. If we can give it some time, the future development will be very promising.

Highway Achievements

The most important construction in Shaanxi Province is highways, because transportation is blocked, the local areas are closed, and all construction is difficult to carry out. The Xianyu Road and the Fenglong Road are sponsored by the province. The former runs from Xianyang North to Yulin on the border of Sui, running through the province, with a length of more than 500 kilometers. The latter runs from Fengxiang to Long County on the border of Gansu, with a length of more than 130 kilometers. Both roads started construction two months ago and are under construction. Another highway from Hanzhong to Beihe, also more than 500 kilometers long, was ordered by Chairman Chiang to be built. The central government has allocated more than 900,000 yuan for expenses and will start construction soon.

Xi'an Municipal Administration

The municipal administration of Xi'an is also being actively carried out. Three important roads in the city have been completed. The original earth roads are now being rebuilt. It is planned to convert all important thoroughfares in the city into stone roads before February of next spring. The provincial government has also decided to establish the Xi'an Electric Power Co., Ltd., with the government and merchants each contributing 250,000 yuan as capital. A preparatory committee has been established, and the director of the Construction Department has been appointed to organize it with three gentry and merchants. Director Lei came south this time and brought an electrical expert with him. He will discuss purchasing the old capital power plant motor from the National Construction Commission. After his public affairs in Shanghai are completed, he will go to Beijing to negotiate. The machine can supply 750 kilowatts of electricity, which is sufficient for the city.

Water Conservancy Construction

Director Lei also said that water conservancy construction in Shaanxi Province is very important. Since the provincial authorities and the National Economic Council have formulated detailed measures and proceeded gradually, the Jinghui and Luohui canals have been completed, irrigating more than one million mu of farmland. The provincial government will collect water conservancy donations according to the land and has decided to use this tax exclusively for water conservancy construction, so that water conservancy construction can be independent and proceed gradually. The drought, which is the most difficult thing in Shaanxi Province, can be avoided.

French Minister to China, Mr. Wilden, Returns to China, Arriving in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

Will Stay in Shanghai for Three or Four Days Before Proceeding to Beijing

Greatly Hopes for the Early Signing of the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty

The French Minister to China, Mr. Wilden, who took leave to return to his country in May, has now returned. He arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m. aboard the French postal ship "D'Artagnan," accompanied by his wife and niece. Various important Chinese and foreign figures in Shanghai went to the wharf to welcome him. Details are as follows:

Chinese and Foreign Welcome

Those who went to the wharf to welcome him yesterday afternoon included: Mr. Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, representing Mr. Wang Jingwei, Minister of Foreign Affairs; Mr. Tang Haian, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, representing Mr. Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council; Mr. Geng Jiaji, Secretary, representing Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng; Mr. Li Rongyao, Secretary of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Mr. Wen Huazhou, representing Police Commissioner Wen Hongen; Mr. Wu Kaisheng, former Secretary of the League of Nations, and others. From the foreign community, there were Mr. Chapolain, Director of the Shanghai Postal Service; Mr. Doukartiel, Counselor of the French Legation; Mr. Soussain, Commercial Counselor; Mr. Melia, Consul General in Shanghai; Consul Lacon; Vice Consul Fina; Mr. Gabol, Acting Chief of the French Concession Police, and dozens of reporters from Chinese and foreign newspapers.

Landing Situation

The "D'Artagnan" entered the port at 11:30 a.m. yesterday and docked at the China Merchants Bureau wharf at the Outer Hongqiao at about 1 p.m. Various important Chinese and foreign figures went there to welcome him. Accompanying the minister, besides his wife, was only his niece, Miss Ge Haki. Upon arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Wilden briefly spoke with the Chinese and foreign welcomers on the ship. He disembarked at 2 p.m. and returned to the French Consulate on the Bund to rest.

Minister Wilden's Remarks

Mr. Wilden, wearing a blue wool coat, along with his wife and niece, exchanged greetings with the Chinese and foreign welcomers. Reporters approached him for an interview and a brief conversation. He said that it was not yet possible to predict whether the Sino-French-Vietnamese Commercial Treaty could be signed in the near future, but he greatly hoped that it could be signed soon. After arriving in Shanghai, he planned to stay for three or four days and then go to Beijing, before heading north to Peiping.
