Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Committee for Promoting National Products Held Second Meeting Yesterday

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce held its second meeting of the Committee for Promoting National Products yesterday afternoon at 2 p.m. Twenty-one people attended, including Gui Yanfang, Liu Minzhai, Wu Yunzhai, Xie Pengfei, Wang Jiean, Chen Liangyu, Hu Juewen, Wu Zhihao, Xie Xiaochu, Lu Wenshao, and others. Lu Wenshao was elected chairman, and Zhu Boyuan recorded the minutes. The following important resolutions were passed: (1) Reported on the previous revision of the organizational rules; (2) Committee members of each group will be designated by the chairman separately and then reported; (3) Regarding the proposal to hold industry-specific exhibitions and exhibitions in other cities, it was resolved to convene relevant trade associations related to national products for discussion before proceeding; (6) and (7) were passed; (8) Regarding Mr. Ye Mojun's proposal to request the government to strictly prohibit the use of rayon fabrics to maintain the lifeline of rural areas in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, it was resolved to be handled by the association's compilation and investigation group. The association's organizational outline is appended as follows: Article 1: This committee is organized according to Articles 28 and 35 of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce's charter and Article 2 of the general rules for each committee. Article 2: The purpose of this committee is to promote national products, self-production, self-manufacturing, and self-use, striving to reduce the import of foreign goods and increase the export of domestic products, in order to achieve the goal of saving the country through national products. Article 3: This committee is composed of a list of names proposed by the Standing Committee of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce from among the member representatives and appointed by the Executive Committee, and one committee member is designated as the director. Article 4: The number of members of this committee ranges from twenty-five to thirty-one. Article 5: In addition to the director designated by the Executive Committee of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, this committee also has the following groups: A. General Affairs Group; B. Compilation and Investigation Group; C. Design Group; D. Publicity Group. Article 6: The committee members of each group are mutually elected from among the committee members, and each group has a group leader, who is elected by each group. Article 7: This committee meets twice a month, and when necessary, the director may convene a meeting temporarily. Article 8: Resolutions of this committee require the attendance of more than one-third of the committee members and the consent of more than half of the attending committee members to be implemented. Article 9: After the establishment of this committee, the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce will issue a notice to the affiliated trade associations of each industry to organize branches, and their regulations will be formulated separately. Article 10: Resolutions of this committee will be sent to the Standing Committee of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for decision and implementation. Article 11: This outline will be submitted to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce for record after being passed by this committee, and the same applies to its amendments.

US and East Africa Successively Reject Japanese Goods

The Continental News reports that the trend of the United States and South America rejecting Japanese goods has become increasingly apparent. This news has caused great anxiety among Japanese business circles, as opening up new markets is crucial to the future of Japan's export trade. According to the Japanese Minister to Mexico, the President of Guatemala told an American correspondent traveling in Central America that a few years ago, few Japanese goods were imported into Guatemala, but now they account for the fourth largest share of Guatemala's total imports. Therefore, the government has no choice but to prohibit their continued import. El Salvador recently issued new tariffs, making it impossible for Japanese goods to be imported at all. Nicaragua has recently implemented a policy of prohibiting Japanese goods, and due to internal politics, imports of Japanese goods have begun to decline. The Commercial Counselor of the Japanese Embassy in Washington is currently traveling in Central American countries and has also reported to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs that the United States is experiencing a significant reduction in exports of coffee and bananas, so business is sluggish. They are now trying to prevent the import of Japanese goods in order to conclude a barter agreement with Japan, and are also negotiating a mutual commercial treaty with the United States. According to a report from the Japanese Consul in Mombasa, East Africa, the government of Tanganyika increased the import tax rate on Japanese goods from October 24, and the neighboring governments of Kenya and Uganda will also follow suit. In the first eight months of this year, the total value of Japanese goods imported into these three East African countries reached 13,165,000 Japanese yen.

Jiahe Arrives in Shanghai Today

Wounded Maritime Police Officer Dies in Xiamen

The China Merchants Bureau's Jiahe was hijacked by pirates in Shantou and three crew members were taken away. Besides the business manager Shen Qixiang and the charity worker Li Shaobing, the remaining one was the tally clerk Gao Liangchen. One member of the escort team, Yang Zetian, was shot and killed by the pirates, and another, Wu Jinyin, was wounded. Wu died of his injuries in a Xiamen hospital. Coffins were prepared separately for them in Xiamen. When the Jiahe departed from Shantou, it carried only 1,594 pieces of cargo, with fruit accounting for 868 pieces and ordinary cargo only 720 pieces. The Shanghai office received a telegram from the Shantou branch last night saying, "The Jiahe departed from Shantou this morning. Before departure, a sign was hung on the front cabin stating that, under the orders of the Maritime Administration Bureau, no passengers were to be taken. Now we have received a telegram from Xiamen that the ship was robbed, which is very shocking." If what the Shantou telegram said is true, and the Jiahe did not take passengers when it departed from Shantou, then how did the pirates get on board? This raises a question. Now that the ship has departed from Xiamen to return to Shanghai, it was originally planned to also sail to Wenzhou, but it will no longer go around Ou. It is expected to enter the port today.

Ministry of Finance Promulgates Regulations for Inspecting Stamp Tax

Inspection Locations Limited to Stores

No Interception on the Road or Intrusion into Residences

The Xinhuashe reports that the stamp tax is one of the important compensations for abolishing miscellaneous taxes and reducing surcharges. After the Executive Yuan discussed and decided on the method of allocating subsidies, the Ministry of Finance actively planned for it. However, according to past results of this tax collection, there are many aspects that need to be improved, and in remote and poor areas, there is an unavoidable suspicion of causing harassment. Therefore, when implementing subsidies to local areas, the method of selling stamps was reorganized and changed to postal sales to prevent the evils of contracting and sales quotas. Regulations for inspection methods were also formulated to prevent problems such as missed or insufficient stamping. Regarding the implementation of the review of stamp tax matters, except for the Shanghai Concession, which is still handled according to previous regulations, the remaining areas are all the responsibility of the provincial, municipal, and county governments. However, the procedures to be followed when carrying out stamp tax inspections and how to distribute the fines should be properly regulated to prevent abuses. The Ministry of Finance has now announced thirteen regulations for inspecting stamp tax, which are implemented uniformly in all provinces and cities. The text of the regulations is appended below: Article 1: All inspections of stamps in provinces, cities, and counties, except for the Shanghai Special District, which has separate regulations, shall be handled in accordance with these regulations. Article 2: Each city and county shall be responsible for inspecting stamps, and the provincial stamp and tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus shall send personnel to conduct spot checks, and the Ministry of Finance shall send personnel to supervise from time to time. Article 3: Each city and county shall strictly implement stamp inspections at any time and place, and shall not announce them in advance or grant exemptions out of favor. Article 4: Inspection personnel shall be selected from those who are honest and familiar with tax laws. Article 5: Anyone may report violations of the stamp tax regulations. When inspection agencies or inspection personnel receive the aforementioned report, they shall immediately go to inspect. Article 6: Inspection personnel must carry an inspection certificate issued by the original dispatching agency or an order from the relevant official for identification when performing inspections. Article 7: Inspection personnel shall perform inspections after sunrise and before sunset, and only within stores. They shall not intercept people on the road or intrude into residences. When inspecting, they shall explain the matter to the person concerned in a peaceful manner and order them to hand over the documents that should be stamped for inspection. They shall not act rashly. Article 8: For documents stored in boxes, the person concerned shall be ordered to open them and take them out for inspection. If they resist, they shall be persuaded earnestly. If they still refuse, they may be forced to comply. Article 9: For documents seized that violate the stamp tax regulations, the inspection personnel shall fill out a receipt stating the name and quantity of the documents and give it to the person concerned. After the case is sent to the judicial organ (including the local court or the county government that also handles judicial affairs, the same below) for a ruling, they shall be returned or confiscated separately. Article 10: For documents seized that violate the stamp tax regulations, the inspection personnel shall state the location of the seizure, the name of the inspected business, the name and quantity of the documents, and the facts of the violation in a report, and submit it along with the documents to the original competent authority for verification, and then forward it to the judicial organ for trial in accordance with the "Revised Rules for Judicial Organs to Impose Penalties and Implement the Stamp Tax Provisional Regulations." If documents that violate the stamp tax regulations are seized from other provinces, cities, or counties, they shall be submitted to the original competent authority for verification and forwarded to the competent judicial organ for summons and trial. Article 11: If the city or county government exerts extraordinary effort in carrying out inspections and achieves significant results, the Ministry of Finance shall recommend to the competent official that they be given a commendation. If the inspection is ineffective and affects tax revenue, the Ministry of Finance shall recommend to the competent official that they be severely punished. Article 12: The fines imposed by judicial organs for cases that violate the stamp tax regulations shall be handled in accordance with Article 6 of the "Revised Rules for Judicial Organs to Impose Penalties and Implement the Stamp Tax Provisional Regulations." If there is an informant, 40% of the fine shall be used as a reward. If there is no informant, 20% shall be used to subsidize the office expenses of the seizing agency, and 20% shall be awarded to the personnel who exerted effort in the inspection. Article 13: If inspection personnel accept bribes, cover up violations, impose penalties without authorization, or engage in other dereliction of duty, they shall be immediately handed over to the judicial organ for investigation and prosecution in accordance with the law once discovered or accused and verified to be true. Article 14: If there are any matters not covered by these regulations, the Ministry of Finance may amend them at any time. Article 15: These regulations shall take effect from the date of promulgation.

Haining Drought Relief Association Cables Zhejiang Province to Request Suspension of Debt Collection

The Haining Drought Relief Association sent a special telegram requesting a stop to the urgent collection of old land taxes by the Zhejiang Provincial Government. It also asked fellow villagers to work hard to raise donations to help the starving refugees. Details are as follows:

Telegram to Provincial Government Requesting Suspension of Debt Collection

The association telegraphed Lu Dipin, Chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting a suspension of the collection of old debts to alleviate the people's suffering. The telegram read: "Chairman Lu and Director Wang of the Zhejiang Provincial Government: The drought situation in Haining this year is the most serious in the province and has long been understood. We are currently raising funds and joining forces with various charitable organizations in Shanghai to provide relief to the dying refugees. However, we have heard that the county government is urgently collecting old land taxes. Land tax is originally derived from land, and this year there is no harvest. Families with property and farmers are equally suffering, and the people are waiting for relief to survive. It does not seem reasonable to demand that they pay off old debts. The result will only cause disturbances. Therefore, we earnestly request that you quickly order the county to stop collecting taxes to benefit the refugees and alleviate the people's suffering. We are extremely anxious. Chairman Jiang Houyue and Xu Guangpu of the Haining County Drought Relief Association, respectfully."

Widespread Disaster, Insufficient Funds, Striving to Raise Relief

The drought in Haining this year is the most severe among the counties in Jiangnan. The seriousness of the disaster has been repeatedly reported in the newspapers. Recently, the Shanghai office of the Haining County Drought Relief Association has repeatedly requested the China and Foreign Famine Relief Committee, the Red Swastika Society, the China Jisheng Society, and the Bodhi Dharma Society to send Li Yunmen, Zheng Shouchun, Zhao Yulin, and Chen Meiqing as directors to lead relief workers to identify areas and provide emergency relief. The various districts are currently being investigated. However, the office of the association in Shanghai and charitable organizations such as the China and Foreign Famine Relief Committee have repeatedly received reports from the directors of various relief efforts stating that the disaster is widespread and funds are insufficient. They are urgently requesting increased relief funds to be remitted to Haining as soon as possible. The situation is extremely urgent. The China and Foreign Famine Relief Committee and the Jisheng Society have decided to increase the remittance to save people's lives. However, the funds for this emergency relief from the association, apart from the 30,000 yuan remaining from the Renchen relief, are mainly temporary loans from the banking sector by Chairman Xu Shenru. There are really no funds to increase. The winter and spring relief efforts are approaching in an instant, making it even more difficult to continue. It is said that the association has now formulated forms and sent letters to fellow villagers in Shanghai, Beijing, Tianjin, Pinghan, Suzhou, and Hangzhou to report on the amount of funds already raised and to continue to work hard to raise funds to save their hometown and benefit the refugees.

Accountants Association Submits Petition to Mandate Registration of Financial Institutions

Strict Supervision to be Implemented

The Shanghai Accountants Association, in light of the recent frequent bankruptcies of financial institutions such as banks, which have had a significant impact on society, and the fact that some have not registered according to the law, making it impossible to investigate beforehand and providing no guarantee afterward, implicating depositors and shaking merchants, causing unimaginable harm, has specially submitted a petition to the Ministries of Finance and Industry, as well as the Shanghai Bureau of Social Affairs, requesting that registration be mandated according to the law and that strict supervision be implemented at all times to prevent problems. The original petition is recorded below. The petition states that recently, bankruptcies of financial institutions such as banks have been frequently heard, having a deep and significant impact on society. Therefore, it is requested that strict supervision be implemented to prevent problems. The association has passed a resolution at a members' meeting that businesses such as banks, trust companies, silver companies, savings associations, and life insurance are of utmost importance to society. In recent years, bankruptcies of banks and trust companies have occurred one after another, implicating depositors and shaking merchants. The reasons for their failure are either unsound organization or illegal operation, and some have not even registered according to the law, indicating a perfunctory attitude from the beginning and an inevitable neglect of operations. If this continues, the harm will be incalculable. The members of the association are responsible for commercial matters and should uphold the government's intention to bring commercial affairs into order and seek remedies for deficiencies. Therefore, it is proposed to petition the Ministries of Finance and Industry and the Shanghai Bureau of Social Affairs to strictly investigate the organization of financial businesses in various places. Those who have not registered shall be ordered to register, otherwise they shall be strictly punished. Even those who have already registered should be subject to strict supervision at all times to maintain standards and prevent problems before they occur. If accountants are needed to assist, they should perform their duties to fulfill the mission of serving society. The newspaper reported that the Ministry of Finance has consulted with the Shanghai Municipal Government, ordering unregistered banks to register according to regulations, and ordering the Bankers Association to refuse membership to unregistered banks. This shows the government's clear understanding and attention to detail. We are greatly impressed and admired. However, the business operations of trust companies, silver companies, savings associations, life insurance, and other industries, although slightly different from those of banks, are essentially the same in terms of attracting deposits. Once an unfortunate event occurs, it is enough to disrupt the financial market and endanger commerce. Therefore, they should all be ordered to register in order to prevent problems before they occur. Furthermore, attention should also be paid to the method of supervision at all times. It cannot be said that once registered, crises can be avoided. Therefore, it is essential to strictly define the responsibility of those who submit annual reports and find effective ways to conduct random inspections. By leveraging the authority of government orders, their norms can be corrected, the financial resources of merchants and the public will not be implicated, and the reputation of the financial sector will be enhanced. Our humble opinion may or may not be appropriate. We hereby submit this petition to your department for adoption and implementation to stabilize the commercial market and benefit the public.

Female Journalist Wang Xiaomeng Returns Home Yesterday

Eloquently Discusses the Radical Nature of the American Women's Movement

According to the Kuo Wen News Agency, Miss Wang Xiaomeng, after graduating from Shanghai University in 1931, worked as the Women's Column Editor for the English-language "China Press". Last summer, she went to the United States at her own expense, hoping to further her studies. She was then admitted to the University of Southern California, and this summer, she obtained a Master's degree in journalism. After leaving the United States, she traveled around Europe, her footprints covering the globe, incidentally investigating the progress of women's movements in various countries. At the beginning of October, she took an Italian mail ship back to China, arriving in Shanghai yesterday morning. Dong Xianguang, the general manager of "China Press," along with friends, went to the ship to greet her. The reporter from the Kuo Wen News Agency met Miss Wang yesterday at her residence on Avenue Joffre. She graciously received them and discussed the radical nature of the American women's movement. She briefly mentioned that in the United States, both men and women receive a considerable education from an early age, and when they grow up, they think of becoming independent to break away from their parents. They boldly seek results, not only obtaining various careers and political power but also gaining extreme trust in society. Every woman, in addition to possessing life skills, has an efficiency in doing things that surpasses that of men. They can be completely economically independent, but most women do not like to marry, nor do they like to have children or manage household affairs. Even if they have children, the feelings between women are very distant. However, they are naturally fond of cleanliness, and very few use servants. Their residences are all spotless. Regarding husbands, the economic boundaries between the two parties are extremely strict. After marriage, each spends what they have for their own use, and there is no mixing. If they marry in the morning and disagree in the evening, they will divorce immediately. On the women's side, they feel that they can socialize freely after divorce, so most women enter social service, and men often take care of housework. Women are extremely strict with themselves because they must first be upright themselves, and their words and deeds must be meticulous to gain the trust and respect of society. Therefore, the status of women is also very solid. Germany is completely the opposite. Hitler and Mussolini, almost in words and deeds, both believe that the love of a mother and child is greater than any force and is also easy to approach, and they claim that to enrich the country, one must first strengthen the people, and to strengthen the people, one must first have good national physiques. They unanimously advocate that women should not participate in politics or enter society but should focus on managing household affairs so that children can receive a good education, which is the opposite of the American advocacy. However, each has its advantages and disadvantages. Things for people all have the needs of an era, with no absolute good and no absolute bad, etc. As for Miss Wang's return to China, she is extremely exhausted from the journey and plans to take a short rest. Whether she will return to work at "China Press" or teach is currently undecided.

The China Manufacturing Oil Factory in Shanghai, in view of the fact that a large number of automobile lubricating oil ("machine oil") is imported every year, and now that highway transportation in various provinces is developed, long-distance buses are flourishing, and in Shanghai, private cars, taxis, and moving and freight cars are also increasing day by day, this drain on China's economy is quite significant. After careful research, they have created a "Castor Leaf" brand of automobile lubricating oil to replace imported goods and save economic rights. Here is a transcription of their original letter: "Dear Sirs, according to our fellow townsman Xiao Xiangang, the amount of imported oil is a serious drain on our country's resources. Now, the China Manufacturing Oil Factory has produced a "Castor Leaf" brand of automobile lubricating oil, which is refined from domestic castor seeds, rapeseed, and other vegetable oils. The oil is thin and has a natural strong adhesion, which makes it difficult for the machinery to heat up and accumulate dirt. It can protect the parts, and it can save the trouble of changing the thickness in winter and summer. The oil consumption is low and the efficiency is high, which is completely different from imported mineral oil. It is the only good product in China. Now it is managed by Yongda Machine Oil Company. Promote it to prevent financial losses," etc. It has been found that the current automobile oil is imported. Because of the need for transportation, it has contributed to the economic invasion of foreigners, which is very painful. Now that there is domestic lubricating oil available for substitution, we should work together to promote it so as to avoid the outflow of money. According to the previous situation in the letter, we hereby urgently write to you to vigorously promote it and put it into practice. The future of domestic products is truly dependent on you." This is truly good news for the domestic goods industry.

Two Detectives Pretend to Be Detectives and Extort Money from Second-Hand Goods Dealers

Writing Loan Notes with Savage Intent

Second-Hand Goods Dealers are Frightened and Move

Guo Tingfu, a Yangzhou native residing at No. 101 Mill Street in the French Concession, is 50 years old this year. He has been engaged in the business of selling second-hand goods or receiving stolen goods for resale. This was learned by Hua Bu Wu Guijin (32 years old, Qingjiang native) of No. 282 of the McLean Police Station (i.e., the Big Ben) and Hua Bu Tang Jingen (35 years old, Jiangbei native) of No. 63. The two patrolmen colluded with each other. On the afternoon of the 28th of last month at about 4:00 PM, Wu and Tang took advantage of their off-duty time, wore plain clothes, and went to Guo's residence together, pretending to be detectives, claiming to be searching. At that time, Guo happened to be out. The two patrolmen Wu and Tang went to Guo's bedroom on the third floor and searched. Then, under the bed, they found four bars of soap and strongly pointed out that Guo had received stolen goods. They ordered Guo's roommate Wan Youming to ask Guo's son to call Guo Tingfu home. After Guo Tingfu returned home, the two patrolmen Wu and Tang insisted on taking Guo to the police station for investigation, otherwise, he would have to pay 100 yuan to settle the matter. At that time, Guo told them that this soap was entrusted to him by a friend to bring back to Jiangbei, but Wu and others ignored it. Later, Guo, in order to avoid trouble, paid 5 yuan, and entrusted Wan Youming to pay Wu and Tang, but the two patrolmen refused and still wanted to take him to the police station. Guo was anxious and asked Wan to temporarily guarantee that he would find a way to raise money. The two patrolmen then agreed that Wan and Guo would meet at the Da Zhong Restaurant at the corner of Zhengjia Bridge and Edward Road that evening to negotiate a solution. At 1 AM, when Wan and Guo arrived at the Da Zhong Restaurant, only Wu Guijin was there. The three began to negotiate, with Wan speaking on the spot, ordering Guo to pay 60 yuan to settle the matter. However, Guo could not raise this huge amount of money at once. Wu then ordered Guo to issue two loan notes of 30 yuan each, dated August 29 and September 29, stating that they would be repaid in two installments on the 2nd and 9th of this month. Wu also ordered Chen Jinquan, a Yangzhou native and waiter in the hotel, to write the loan notes. Later, Guo and Wan were able to escape, but Guo ultimately made a living as a small vendor. How could he raise this money? He was afraid of the power of the two patrolmen Wu and Tang, so the whole family moved to No. 7 Feijia Lane, Kangdi Road, to hide. When the deadline came, the two patrolmen Wu and Tang went to get the money, but Guo had already moved. They then ordered Wan Youming to hand over Guo Tingfu. At this point, Guo could not bear the harassment, so he and Wan Youming reported to the French police station. After receiving the report, the police chief summoned the two patrolmen to the case and found a similar loan note on each of them. He reported the matter to the chief patrolman, who dismissed and detained the two patrolmen. He also sent detective Wang Rusong and detective Wang Dongwan to find out the whole story of the case. Yesterday afternoon, the two patrolmen were sent to the First Criminal Court of the Special Second Court, where Judge Li Changnian conducted the interrogation. The police station lawyer Gu Shouxi explained the case, accusing them of the crimes of intimidation and dereliction of duty under Articles 370 and 129 of the Criminal Code. Then, the plaintiff Guo Tingfu and the witnesses Wan Youming and Chen Jinquan stated the process of the defendants' extortion and forced loan notes. Detective Wang Dongwan reported the investigation and presented the two loan notes to the court. When Tang Jingen was interrogated, he confessed that he knew Wan Youming. Wan first borrowed 20 yuan from me, and then said that Guo Tingfu also wanted to borrow 20 yuan. Because I had no money, I borrowed it from Wu Guijin. Because Wu has always lent money, Wan invited Guo to voluntarily issue a loan note of 30 yuan including interest. There was no search for soap or extortion. I was falsely accused, and I asked for investigation. When Wu Guijin was questioned, his confession was the same as Tang's, and he hired lawyer Wang Shizong to defend him. The court verified the confession, announced the end of the debate, and scheduled the sentence for the 10th. The two defendants were returned to custody.

Sun Temple Lawsuit

Former Resident Receives Criminal Punishment

New Resident Cannot Take Over

The Sun Temple on Datong Road in Zhabei was founded in the fifth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, built by the female lay Buddhist Jiang Dexian, who raised funds from local people. It is purely local public property and has always been managed by monks selected by donors and local gentry. Recently, the abbot of the temple, Yuejin, suddenly received criminal punishment due to a flower fair, so he was stripped of his abbot qualification and the Sun Temple was returned to the donors. The donors, including He Liandi, then elected the monk Ruhai as the abbot of the temple. He was scheduled to take over on July 25 of this year, but unexpectedly, the monk Ziyan, who claimed to be the abbot, refused to hand over the temple. The former abbot, the old monk Lingyan, then filed a criminal self-accusation with the local court against Ziyan for attempting to seize the temple, requesting a thorough investigation and attaching a private accusation. As a result, Ziyan was sentenced to 30 days of detention, and the property of the Sun Temple was handed over to the plaintiff for management. Ziyan refused to accept the verdict and filed an appeal in the second instance, claiming that it was a civil legal relationship and did not give rise to criminal issues. Now, the monk Ruhai hired lawyer Peng Xuehai to file a lawsuit with the local court to confirm his identity, requesting that the defendant monk Ziyan be ordered to hand over the Sun Temple for management to protect public property. The object of the lawsuit is to confirm the plaintiff as the abbot of the Sun Temple, stating that the defendant Ziyan is the disciple of the monk Xianbang. Xianbang died in 1926, and Xiande became the abbot, squandering almost all of the temple's property. Fearing that the gentry donors would question him, he fled to Taizhou in 1929. At that time, the defendant left the Sun Temple and went out. Other monks could not maintain it, so they obtained the consent of the gentry donors and hired the monk Lingyan of Yuantong Temple to serve concurrently as the abbot of the Sun Temple. After Lingyan took over, he paid off the debts and repaired the temple, achieving good results. Later, because of old age, he could not take care of it, so he sent the monk Yuejin as the abbot. Later, because Yuejin was reported for flower fair relations, he was punished. Therefore, the temple was returned to the donor He Liandi, who was then elected by the local gentry as the abbot of the temple, and a temple board of directors was formally established to manage the temple property and reported to the Public Security Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau for registration on file. The Sun Temple was built by the female lay Buddhist Jiang Dexian who raised funds, and it has always been managed by the donor He Liandi. This is an undisputed fact by both parties. Therefore, the Sun Temple is local public property, and no one can claim private ownership, which is undoubtedly beyond doubt, etc. After receiving the submission, the court held a special hearing in the Fourth Tribunal yesterday morning by Judge Chen Wenkai. The plaintiff, monk Ruhai, did not arrive, and his agent, lawyer Peng Xuehai, arrived, stating Ruhai's age as 42, from Hubei, and the grounds for the lawsuit, requesting confirmation that the plaintiff was the abbot of the Sun Temple. Then, the witnesses He Liandi and the monk Lingyan testified everything. The judge obtained the confession and adjourned the hearing to a later date because the defendant did not arrive.

Zhu Ziyun is Not Guilty

Two Medical Organizations Provide Written Proof

Pulse and Medicine Match, Medicine Dosage is Not Excessive

Zhu Ziyun, a traditional Chinese medicine pediatrician and ENT specialist from Jiangwan, was recently sued by Cai Ziying, a Yangzhou native, who hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court, accusing him of causing death due to negligence. Judge Wu Zehan of the First Special Court has summoned him twice, and the details have been published in this newspaper. At 11:30 yesterday morning, Judge Wu summoned him again in the Third Criminal Court. Zhu Ziyun hired lawyer Lu Qi to defend him. The court then handed the prescription submitted by the plaintiff to Zhu for review, asking whether it was his prescription. Zhu replied yes. The court also asked whether the plaintiff's child, Shunbao, had given him Ma Yuanyuan's previous prescription to review when he came to see the doctor. He replied, no, and claimed that according to the usual practice of doctors, if the first prescription is not correct, the direction must be changed. Now, the three prescriptions I prescribed are all the same, which shows that there was no change after taking the medicine, etc. The court then summoned the witness Zhou Shaoyu to the case. According to his confession, on July 26 of this year, he was invited by Dr. Dong to diagnose and treat the plaintiff's child. At that time, the child was already in great danger and it was impossible to save him. According to the plaintiff, after taking Dr. Zhu's medicine, the child's condition changed greatly. The court then handed the three prescriptions prescribed by Zhu Ziyun to Zhou for review, asking whether the pulse case and the prescription were consistent. He replied that the pulse case and the medicine were completely consistent and there was no discrepancy. However, when I went to see the doctor, the child's condition was completely hot, etc. Then, Ma Mingyuan reported to the case and testified that the plaintiff's child, because he had measles, was diagnosed and treated by me on June 8. The last time I diagnosed and treated him was on July 15. The child's measles had healed and still needed conditioning. Unexpectedly, he started eating meat too early, which caused him to become ill again. The court then handed Song's three prescriptions to him for review, asking whether the pulse case and the medicine were consistent and whether the medicine dosage was too heavy. He replied that it was consistent and the medicine dosage should be determined according to the severity of the disease, etc. Judge Wu then announced that the court had sent a letter to the Shenzhou Medical Association and the China National Medicine Association for identification. The two associations convened various medical groups in the city on the 4th of this month for discussion and replied to the court, stating that the pulse and medicine of Zhu Ziyun's prescription were consistent and the medicine dosage was not excessive. The reply letter was also issued to both parties for review. The court then ordered the debate to begin. The plaintiff's lawyer expressed dissatisfaction with the identification and requested that the Central National Medicine Museum be re-identified. Judge Wu believed that there was no need for re-identification and ruled to reject the application. The plaintiff's lawyer declared an appeal. Judge Wu ruled that the ruling could not be appealed according to law. Then, after the lawyers from both sides began to debate, the court ruled that the debate was over and the verdict was set to be announced. Zhu Ziyun is not guilty.

Horrifying News: Attempted Murder of a Brother for Property

The Chauffeur of Huang Jinrong Narrowly Escapes an Ambush

Xu Xiaodu Actually Enters into a Contract to Kill His Brother

Xu Guilin, a local resident, currently 40 years old, works as a chauffeur for Huang Jinrong, the owner of the Great World theater. He lives at No. 11, Lane 54, Gordon Road. His parents are deceased, but they left behind three siblings, including Guilin, and eighteen old and new houses on Gordon Road, valued at tens of thousands of dollars. After the death of their parents, the houses were divided into three equal shares, with Guilin, his younger brother Xiaodu (also known as Jiantang), and the youngest brother, Guisheng, each receiving six houses. Unfortunately, Guisheng passed away due to illness on the eighth day of the first month of the lunar calendar this year, and all of his property had been sold to Guilin before his death. Xu Xiaodu, on the other hand, did not engage in any productive work, and gradually sold off all of his houses. Recently, Xiaodu repeatedly asked his brother Guilin for loans, but was refused. As a result, a malicious thought arose in his mind. He colluded with Wang Gensheng and others from Nanxiang to kill Guilin, hoping to inherit his property. However, because

The plan was not kept secret, someone reported it to Detective Ma Jinbiao of the Putuo Road Police Station. On the evening before last, at around 9 p.m., he, along with Detective Chief Shi Enjian, Detective Xu Huanqing, and Bailiff Zhao Zifang, apprehended Xu Xiaodu and Wang Gensheng. They also seized a wood-chopping knife and a written contract, and brought them to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. According to the police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, in addition to prosecuting the two defendants, Xu and Wang, for attempted murder under Article 383, Paragraph 4 of the Criminal Law, he also detailed the circumstances of the case. He stated that the defendant Xu Xiaodu and the victim Xu Guilin were brothers who each inherited a certain amount of ancestral property. Guilin, through diligence and thrift, increased his wealth, while Xiaodu did not engage in any productive work and sold off all of his family property, leading him to repeatedly ask Guilin for loans. On several occasions, he was refused, and he harbored resentment in his heart. In August of this year, he discussed with Wang Gensheng the idea of

Finding a way to kill his brother, so that he could inherit his brother's property worth 70,000 yuan. If the plan succeeded, he would pay a reward of 2,000 yuan. Wang, unwilling to do it himself, agreed to find a reliable person. Later, Wang discussed it with his friend Chen Qiuquan, as Chen and Wang both worked as laborers in the Shenxin No. 9 Factory. Chen agreed to a reward of 1,000 yuan if the plan succeeded. At the time, Chen did not commit himself, only saying that he would consider it further. Therefore, Chen, on the 30th of last month, discussed it at length with his sworn brother, Sha Mapi. They both believed that this matter involved human life, and the responsibility was great, and advised Chen not to do it. They also feared that if Chen refused, Wang Gensheng would inevitably find someone else to carry out the plan. Therefore, they immediately reported it to Chinese Detective Ma Jinbiao, who reported it to the police station. At that time, the police station, believing that it was only necessary to warn the two defendants, did not arrest them. Instead, they devised a plan, instructing Sha Mapi to contact Wang and

Pretend to agree to his request. Wang was satisfied upon hearing this. On the evening before last, at 9 p.m., Xu Xiaodu, Wang Gensheng, and Sha Mapi went together to Room 26 of the Zhongxing Hotel at No. 64, Lane 234, Ma Bai Road. Xu used the alias Wang Jiantang and discussed the method of carrying out the plan. Sha asked Xu how much the reward would be. Xu replied 2,000 yuan. At that time, they drew up a written contract, and Xu and Wang both signed and affixed their fingerprints to it. The contract stated that if Xu Guilin was killed, a reward of 2,000 yuan would be paid, otherwise the contract would be void. After the contract was completed, Wang went outside to Zhou Shaogen's tailor shop at No. 1075, Macau Road, and falsely claimed that he was chopping firewood, so he managed to get a knife and took it back to give to Sha Mapi.

Instructing him to carry out the plan. At that time, the detectives outside the door followed and entered, arresting them. The contract was verified to be in Xu's handwriting, and the contract and knife were presented as evidence. Subsequently, the witness Sha Mapi and the victim Xu Guilin submitted reports proving everything. When questioned, Xu Xiaodu initially gave evasive answers, but later admitted without hesitation that he intended to harm his brother. Because Guilin had swallowed his younger brother Guisheng's houses, he wanted to kill him. Wang Gensheng also confessed that he was entrusted by Xu to find Chen Qiuquan. The court then appointed lawyer Fan Gang to cross-examine the police station's lawyer. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the confession and sentenced Xu Xiaodu to three years of imprisonment for preparing to kill a collateral relative, and Wang Gensheng to two years of imprisonment for assisting in preparing to kill a collateral relative. The contract was confiscated.

A Small and Winding Printing Shop

Cannot be Reached Without Passing Through Many Houses

Surprisingly, a Small Operation Employs a Printer as a Watchman

—A Forged Match Coupon Leads to a Breakthrough—

Recently, the Ruilun Tobacco Company on Kaifeng Road, in order to promote its business, has been attaching gift coupons to its company brand cigarettes. The lowest value coupon is a match coupon. Any customer who obtains such a coupon can go to a nearby tobacco shop and exchange it for a box of matches. To protect the business of the tobacco shops, if a tobacco shop accumulates 1,000 match coupons, it can exchange them for seven yuan in cash from the company. However, Ruilun Company recently discovered that someone was privately manufacturing company brand match gift coupons, so it paid special attention. Until the 30th of last month, Zhang Zhilin, Shi Pengcheng, Tong Quanyuan, Chen Shunrong, and others went to redeem cash with forged coupons and were reported to the Concession Police Station. Detectives were dispatched to arrest them and they were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. This was reported in this newspaper. The day before yesterday, Gu Jieqing from Pudong also brought 30 forged coupons to a tobacco shop at No. 29, Baoyu Lane, French Concession, to exchange for matches. He was discovered and reported to the French police, who arrested Gu. Since there was already a case in the Public Concession, the Concession Police Station was notified and dispatched Detective Chief Shang Wu and Detective Ji Xiuquan to bring Gu back. They investigated the source of the forged coupons. Gu confessed that they were given to him by his brother, Gu Jiezhen. The detectives went to No. 57, Hengmao Lane, Mintini Road, to arrest Gu Jiezhen. Gu then led them to No. 12, Wenyuan Fang, on the same road, where they seized a large number of forged coupons, totaling 300,000. Gu Jiezhen confessed that the coupons were printed at the Damei Printing Shop run by Xu Heyun at No. 35, Lane 113, Lafayette Road. The Chinese and Western detectives went to arrest Xu, but did not find any forged coupons. They then went to No. 47, Lane 551, Xinzha Road, and found three lead plates. The lead plates were sent by Xu, intending to destroy the evidence. The lead plates were full of the image of the forged coupon, fearing that the matter would be exposed, so they were sent to be destroyed. The back of the lead plates had the words "Damei" on them, and they were all brought back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, along with the four previously arrested, Zhang Zhilin, etc., they were all sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the above circumstances and declared that the structure of Xu Heyun's printing shop was very strange. The main door was usually closed, and people entered and exited through a side door. A printer was hired as a watchman. In order to reach the printing area of the printing shop, one had to pass through many winding houses. There was only a very small machine and a paper cutter. The scale was not large, so why hire a printer as a watchman? The appearance was very suspicious. It was actually an organization specializing in manufacturing various forged coupons. Because the police station still needed to investigate the case, it requested a postponement. The Ruilun Tobacco Company engaged lawyer Tang Mingshi to represent the defendant Xu Heyun, while lawyer Fan Gang was engaged to defend him. After a brief interrogation by the court, it was ordered to postpone the interrogation to another date. The defendants were returned to detention.

The Accountant of the Fresh Pork Industry Association Falsely Reports a Theft and Embezzles Funds

Yang Weixin is Extremely Foolish

Detectives Ascertain the Truth

Yesterday afternoon at around 2 p.m., Yang Weisheng, the accountant of the Fresh Pork Industry Association in Sunjia Lane, inside the Dadongmen (age 25, from Shaoxing), suddenly went to the 16th Concession Branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau to report that at around 10 a.m. today (yesterday), he was carrying 2,692.18 yuan in public funds. He left the association and walked to the Yuanda Pig Shop in Yong'an Lane, 16th Concession. He first paid 208.96 yuan to the shop and obtained a receipt, then carried the remaining funds and went out. As he was about to deposit the money in the Tonghe Bank on Limalu Road, he unexpectedly encountered two men he did not recognize at the entrance of Tiemao Lane on Xianhua Street. They greeted him and led him into the lane. The two men suddenly took out pistols from their sides and threatened him, forbidding him to make a sound. At the same time, they took all the 2,485.22 yuan in paper money from his pocket and fled with the stolen goods. At that time, he knew he had been robbed and was stunned. After a while, he regained his composure and immediately reported to the chairman of the association, Xin Zhouxiang, and then came to the bureau to report. He requested that the robbers be pursued. The bureau, because Yang's report had many suspicious points, and it was unlikely that there would be such a foolish person who would carry a large sum of money and follow strangers into a small alley when greeted on the street, immediately dispatched team leader Dong Mingde and Han Ruisheng, along with detectives Yuan Haishan, Yu Maolong, and Yuan Mingcai, to investigate. They learned that Yang Weisheng was fond of pleasure and often went to Tianyun Lou and other entertainment venues to seek pleasure, and because he was addicted to opium, his monthly salary was not enough. He had no choice but to privately use more than 600 yuan of public funds. In desperation, he came up with a strange idea. On the 5th of this month, after collecting 2,485.22 yuan in membership fees from various members, he secretly took 285.22 yuan from it to repay the money he had spent, and hid the remaining 2,200 yuan behind the bed curtains in the mezzanine of the wall, for future use. Then, yesterday, he first sent 206.96 yuan of other public funds to the Yuanda Pig Shop, and then lingered for a long time in the Xianhua Street area of Xiaodongmen, and then rushed to the Changyuan Pig Shop to falsely report the robbery to Xin Zhouxiang, the chairman of the association. They immediately rushed to the Fresh Pork Industry Association in Sunjia Lane and found 2,200 yuan of stolen money in the wall behind Yang's bed. He then reported the information to the branch director Guan Gong, and then brought Yang Weisheng to trial. He confessed everything after questioning. Because it involved embezzlement of public funds and falsely reporting a robbery, he was ordered to prepare a document and send it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Careless Fire on the Third Floor of Jin Hua Foreign Firm Warehouse

Wool Stored Inside Completely Destroyed

Yesterday afternoon at around 9 p.m., a fire suddenly broke out on the second floor of the Jin Hua Foreign Firm warehouse at No. 60, Sichuan Road and Guangdong Road. By the time street patrolmen noticed it, the fire was already out of control, and flames were bursting out of the windows. Fortunately, the Central Fire Brigade received the alarm and rushed fire trucks to the scene to put out the fire. However, at that time, it was already a raging fire and it was impossible to enter. A ladder was raised and water was sprayed from the outside. After more than two hours, the fire was gradually extinguished. As a result, the second floor of the warehouse was completely burned, and the wool stored inside was completely destroyed. The loss was considerable. The cause of the fire is still unclear and is currently under investigation.

Tragic Death of a Child Laborer

Right Arm Severed by Machine Belt

Died Tragically After Ineffective Treatment at the Hospital

Ji Zhengyuan, a child from Haimen, currently 15 years old, lived at No. 15, Lane 70, Xiaoshadu Road. He worked as a laborer in the roving department of the Puyi Yarn Factory at No. 8, Robison Road. Yesterday evening at around 7 p.m., a belt on the machine fell down. The machine manager, Jiang Guisheng, was lazy and ordered Ji Zhengyuan to drag the belt onto the iron hook. The motor was humming. Ji's right arm was caught in the belt and severed instantly. He lost consciousness. He was sent to the Baolong Hospital for treatment, but died at 10 p.m. After the hospital reported it to the Putuo Road Police Station, a detective was ordered to investigate and the body was sent to the coroner's office for examination.

There are Two Morphine Dens in the French Concession

One on Rue Luber and One on Rue Wantz

Extremely Large Scale, Not Comparable to Ordinary Ones

—Two People Detained by the Public Concession Pending Trial—

Yesterday afternoon, Feng Zhiming, the Chinese detective chief of the Narcotics Department of the General Police Station, Detective Bao Liansheng, and Western Detective Hale, successively arrested Shan Tinggui from Changzhou and Cong Shengjiu from Fengtian, two private morphine traffickers, at No. 33, Qingchang Lane, Avenue Emile Zola. One tael of morphine, a small sample package, many lead rings, seals, envelopes, and other items were seized. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. The Public Works Department, because the main culprit He Xinbo was at large and the organization had not been investigated, did not prosecute Shan and Cong, but only requested permission to detain them. According to the police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, the police station received a report yesterday that someone was selling morphine at No. 33, Lane 396 (Qingchang Lane), Avenue Emile Zola. He reported this to the court and obtained a search warrant. At 4 p.m., he first sent female detective Zhou Huici to contact Shan, wanting to buy ten taels of morphine. Shan said that the morphine was stored elsewhere. To buy ten taels, it would cost 230 yuan, and the goods would be delivered at 5:30 p.m. He gave her a sample package of morphine, which Zhou took away. At 5:30 p.m., he and the Chinese and Western detectives went and waited outside the door. Detective Zhou entered first. Shan said that because the money had not been paid, he would only give one tael first, and the other nine taels would be given after the money was paid. At that time, the detectives rushed in and arrested Shan. Soon after, Cong Shengjiu arrived and was also arrested. Cong confessed that he went to No. 17, Ba'an Fang, Rue de la Gare, French Concession. The detectives and French police detectives went to search Cong's house but found nothing. Cong then pointed out that the morphine was hidden in the small inn next door at No. 16. They went to search and found only many lead rings. These lead rings were used on leather shoes. However, the sample given to the female detective by Shan had this kind of lead ring nailed to the envelope, and the words "Remember the Chrysanthemum" were printed on it. When asked where the morphine came from, he said that he got it from He Xinbo, who lived at No. 53, Wanyi Fang, Rue Luber, and whose wholesale point was at No. 19, Yongji Lane, Rue Wantz. The police station went to investigate these two places, but the organizations set up there were extremely large and not comparable to ordinary ones. He requested permission to detain them for investigation. According to the detectives' report, when questioned, Shan Tinggui and others confessed to selling morphine and earning one yuan per tael. Judge Wu Tingqi reviewed the confession and ordered that Shan and Cong be detained for seven days for further interrogation.

Oriental Trust Company Sues Fang Liujun, Etc. for Repayment of Debt

Defendant Fails to Appear for Trial

The Court Orders a Rescheduled Hearing

According to the Guowen News Agency, the Oriental Trust Company at No. 462 Fujian Road went out of business on May 10 of this year and declared liquidation on May 21. Lawyer Zhang Shijie and accountant Qin Yanzhao were appointed as liquidators, with full power to handle all liquidation matters. It was found that Fang Liujun, the owner of the Dachang Military Uniform and Leather Goods Shop at No. 5, Lane 6, Deqing Lane, Moore Road, had borrowed 3,000 yuan in national currency from the company on April 10 of this year, agreeing to repay it on June 10 of this year. Fang Jiaobo was responsible for guaranteeing it, and a promissory note was made as evidence. However, it was not repaid when due. The handler Zou Rangqing (manager of the Oriental Trust Company) lent the money because he fully trusted Fang Jiaobo's guarantee, so he did not even verify the address of the Dachang Shop. Later, after repeated urging from lawyer Zhang Shijie, Fang Jiaobo was uncooperative. It was not until recently that Fang told the address of the Dachang Shop. The liquidators Zhang Shijie and others sent a special letter to Fang Liujun, the owner of the Dachang Shop, on October 13, ordering him to repay the debt within a time limit. However, after half a month, there was no response. Lawyer Zhang believes that the liquidation period of the Oriental Trust Company is about to expire, and all repayments need to be collected as soon as possible in order to close the case. Therefore, he filed a lawsuit with the Shanghai First Special District District Court and requested a declaration of provisional execution. Yesterday afternoon at 3 p.m., Judge Peng Shi summoned the debtor Fang Liujun and guarantor Fang Jiaobo to the fourteenth court, but neither of them appeared in court. Lawyer Zhang Shijie stated the reasons for the lawsuit and presented the defendant's promissory note as evidence. The court ordered that since the defendants were not present today, the defendants would be summoned to court again at 2:10 p.m. on the 17th of this month for further hearing.

The Hongqiao Sanatorium in western Shanghai uses all the latest modern medical equipment. It has plenty of sunlight and air, and a quiet and clean environment. This kind of natural rural life is very suitable for citizens to quit opium. The hospital has set up an addiction treatment department, headed by the son of Mr. Fu Baolie, the resident director of the De Kang Hospital. Those who are financially strapped will not be charged addiction treatment fees in addition to the hospitalization fee.

Exhibition News of Dung Weng's Personal Calligraphy and Seal Carving

Dung Weng, a quirky genius in Shanghai's literary and art circles and recent second-place winner at the Southeast Transportation Expo, has long been renowned for his poetry, calligraphy, and seal carving. He is now holding his third personal calligraphy and seal carving exhibition from the 9th to the 11th of this month at the Lake Society on Beijing Road. On display will be 300 pieces of calligraphy in various styles and 100 copies of seal imprints from the "Three Longs and Two Shorts Studio," all marked for sale. Mr. Dung is one of the most diligent artists of modern times. His calligraphy covers almost all styles, each reaching a high level of attainment. His work in metal and stone reaches the heights of the Tai and Han dynasties, looking down upon Wu Changshuo. Shanghai has always been a hub of culture; it is expected that many will come to appreciate the true art of the Orient. At the same time, the Lake Society is publishing the complete works of Yin Yishi, and Mr. Dung is donating a portion of his works to support it. Additionally, he has obtained paintings from female artists Chen Xiaocui and Gu Qingyao to add to the exhibition, all of which are masterpieces, making this a particularly rare and valuable opportunity.

Publication of "An Outline of Chinese Civil, Criminal, and Commercial Law in English"

Lawyer Hong Shihao's previous English book, "A Section of the Commercial Law of the Republic of China," was widely circulated. He has now continued with a new book, "An Outline of Chinese Civil, Criminal, and Commercial Law," comprising over 300 pages and more than 100,000 words. It includes essential summaries of all current civil, criminal, and commercial laws. Its structure and application draw from the Anglo-American school, with each chapter including illustrative examples and citations of Chinese and foreign theories, as well as over 800 judgments from the Supreme Court, the Supreme Court of Justice, and the Dali Court. Experts such as Wu Jingxiong and British judges have written prefaces, praising it as a creative work on Chinese law in English. All major Western bookstores and Mr. Hong's office are selling it, and sales are said to be very brisk.

Famous Cantonese Opera Troupe to Arrive in Shanghai

The Guangdong Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road has recently hired the Huashan Yu Nv Cantonese Opera Troupe, which will soon arrive to perform. The troupe includes Li Songpo, a civil and military performer whose art is excellent and who is particularly hardworking, making him very popular with audiences. In recent years, he has swept through Guangdong, earning the nickname "Iron Broom." The female lead, Tan Yulan, is a renowned Cantonese opera star, long famous in Guangdong, specializing in romantic dramas, and comparable to the famous actress Tan Lanqing. There is a Cantonese saying, "Two orchids blooming together," which praises both Tans. The troupe also includes the martial performer Sai Zilong, the young male performer Duan Jianchong, and the comedian Peng Xueqiu, all of whom are popular stars of the moment.

Because its sliced herbal medicines are authentic and its refined prescriptions are convenient, many patients are happy to purchase them. Patients in the northern district of Shanghai often go to the general factory on Tongji Road in Zhabei to buy them. Special Feature

The China International Famine Relief Commission's Disaster Prevention Work

Some say that the China International Famine Relief Commission is a disaster relief organization, so why does it pay so much attention to projects such as road construction, river management, and canal repair? When did these projects start to be implemented? What is their value? How do they benefit the people? And how should they be developed? However, upon examining the history of the Commission's founding and the work it has accomplished over the years, one can feel a new force in Chinese society that is gradually increasing, increasing food production and reducing famine. The China International Famine Relief Commission is an important organization in this new force. The construction work it has completed in sixteen provinces over the years has achieved considerable results, so people at home and abroad have provided financial support. The following is a summary of most of the Commission's projects:

History of the Founding: In 1920, a severe drought struck five provinces in North China, and about 20 million people were starving. In the autumn of that year, American Minister Crane initiated a gathering of people from various countries in Beijing to organize the China Relief Committee. Due to Crane's call, the American Red Cross donated one million US dollars. It was agreed that this huge sum would be used for construction work, starting with road construction, implementing work-for-food. Baker was elected as the Director-General to manage work-for-food affairs in Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, and other provinces, and with the full cooperation of the provincial governments and the tireless efforts of the staff, all kinds of difficulties were resolved. At its peak, it employed 35,000 yuan. Food was given according to the work done, and many victims were rescued as a result. The 500-mile automobile road in Shandong Province was built in that year. Work-for-food was originally a trial run by the Commission, but it was completely successful. At the same time, other disaster relief organizations in North China provided emergency relief, saving countless lives, but it was not of a permanent nature. In 1921, after the North China relief work, the Chinese and Western leaders of various relief groups decided to set up a permanent organization, and the China International Famine Relief Commission was established. It was decided to focus more on disaster prevention work and not provide emergency relief unless absolutely necessary. Therefore, work-for-food became the Commission's goal.

Restoring the Old Course of the Yellow River: At the beginning of its establishment, the Commission allocated a large sum of money to the disaster-stricken provinces to carry out construction projects. In 1922, most of the road and embankment works in Shandong and Henan provinces were repaired with the Commission's assistance. In that year, the Yellow River breached its banks in Lijin. The management project required 1.5 million yuan. Dams were made with 40,000 cubic yards of stone, and American pine wood was transported from 100 miles upstream as piles. The breached Yellow River was restored to its old course. At the height of the work, about 15,000 workers were employed. The Commission provided assistance of 360,000 yuan. By 1923, the project was completed. As a result, 200 square miles of submerged land were restored to its original state, and 250,000 displaced victims were able to return to their hometowns.

Relief of the 1924 Flood: In 1924, severe floods struck Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces. The Gan River flooded, and the embankments on both sides were washed away. North of Nanchang, the delta outside the mouth of the Gan River became a large lake. At the same time, the Yangtze River surged down, breaking the Nantang embankment in Shishou, Hubei, and most of the fields were abandoned. North of Hankou was completely submerged. In July, Beijing experienced incessant rain, which was rare in the past 30 years. Mountain torrents erupted in Shanxi Province. Due to this unprecedented rainfall, the embankments of various important rivers in Hebei Province were almost completely destroyed. About 10,000 square miles of land were submerged. The water conservancy bureaus established by the central government and various provinces, as well as the provinces that suffered this disaster, sent letters to the Commission for assistance. The Commission's engineering division made every effort to serve and fulfill its responsibilities. In 1924 and 1925, the Commission was responsible for repairing the embankments in Hebei, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces. The government levied special surcharges, and the Commission's provincial branches also collected these relief funds to carry out various disaster prevention works.

Embankment Repair Project in Hebei, Hubei, and Jiangxi Provinces: In the summer of 1925, the Commission's engineering division carefully built the Shishou Embankment upstream of Hankou, turning long-abandoned fields into fertile fields. It can earn 2 million yuan per year. The labor cost was about 100,000 yuan. In addition, local donations were used to subsidize the civil works. This embankment is covered with stone and is very strong. It can be regarded as a memorial to the Commission's project. In 1927, the Commission had about 20 plans for Hubei's flood control project, costing 1.6 million yuan, half of which was subsidized by the Commission and half was provided by the local government. In the spring of that year, the emergency project of Zhanggong Embankment near Hankou was also repaired, costing 160,000 yuan. In 1925, the Commission repaired many damaged canals and embankments between the Gan River and Poyang Lake. This project cost 200,000 yuan, but the harvest was ten times this number. It can restore the original land value of 20 million yuan. In 1925 and 1926, the Commission planned and managed embankment works in Hebei Province, using 400,000 yuan. In addition to the Commission's engineering personnel, no other organization shared this work. The long embankment in Xidian, 30 miles east of Baoding, and the Qianli Embankment in Yu Wei were all properly repaired by the Commission's engineering division. The following year, the harvest of farmland in that area, in Xidian alone, was worth 5 million yuan. In total, the Commission has completed 904 miles of embankment work in these 12 years. (To be continued)

Sports News

The City's Third Joint Middle School Sports Meet Opens Today

The opening ceremony will be held at 1:00 PM. Mayor Wu will give a speech.

The Municipal Education Bureau has specially dispatched cars to pick up the referees and staff.

More than 900 athletes will gather at Jiaotong University.

The city's third joint middle school sports meet is scheduled to be held at the Jiaotong University track and field today, and the opening ceremony will be held at 1:00 PM. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director Chu Minyi, Director Pan Gongzhan, and Li Zhaohuan will attend the meeting to give speeches. The details are as follows:

Venue Arrangement

The venue for this year's meeting is the track and field of the National Jiaotong University in Xujiahui. The venue has been arranged by the teachers and students of the Jiaotong University's physical education department and the Education Bureau. The main entrance of the venue is on Gaodun Road. The rostrum is set on the east side of the field. The seats for each school are arranged as follows: municipal schools are next to the rostrum, private schools are on the west and south sides, and girls' schools are on the north side. Temporary reed sheds have been set up for male and female athletes to rest. The rostrum is also equipped with wireless broadcasting so that speeches and reports can be heard clearly throughout the venue.

Opening Ceremony in the Afternoon

The opening ceremony will be held at 1:00 PM today. Chairman Wu Tiecheng, Vice Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Honorary Instructors Chu Minyi, and Li Zhaohuan will all attend the meeting to give speeches. The conference has also specially invited music expert Zhong Zitong to attend and guide the singing of the sports meet song. Students from all schools must arrive at the venue before 12:30 PM to prepare. The Education Bureau has also specially prepared cars to pick up the referees at 11:00 AM at the YMCA on North Sichuan Road and at 11:30 AM at the YMCA on Baxianqiao. Lunch will be provided by the conference.

Schools Closed Today

The Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed the public and private middle schools in the city: The city's third joint middle school sports meet has been scheduled to be held for three days starting on the 8th of this month. During the event, schools may close for half a day to visit. Please be informed of this order.

Today's Program

He arrived in Shanghai a few days ago and visited the National Jiaotong University at 2 p.m. yesterday to inspect the entire student military training corps. The details are as follows:

Personnel Present: Director Pan Youqiang, Director of Military Training Association Jiao Jihua, Full-time Member of Military Training Association Ouyang Dingming, Dean of Studies of Jiaotong University Jiu Weiyu, Dean of Students Chen Jiaxun, Deans Zhang Tingjin, Li Qianruo, Hu Duanxing, and over 300 military training students.

Inspection Details: The inspection began at 2 p.m., with Chief Instructor Ouyang Dingming as the commander-in-chief, and assistant instructors He Suting, Li Kanru, Xie Xuan, Wang Shanwu, Ding Zirang, and Wang Dao serving as captains. The entire military training student body was divided into two teams, all dressed in yellow woolen military uniforms, cloth leggings, and white gloves, exhibiting a formidable appearance. The inspection included a review parade, squad drills, neat formations, skilled maneuvers, and evident high morale.

Director's Address: After the inspection, everyone gathered in front of the rostrum, where Director Pan Youqiang delivered an address, stating that compared to his inspection of the student military corps last year, there had been significant progress in achievement and spirit, which he found very gratifying. He emphasized that the effectiveness of implementing military-national education had been proven historically, citing the resurgence of Germany and the strength of Italy as examples. Therefore, national and ethnic organization requires the implementation of military-national education. He expressed his satisfaction with the proficiency and morale displayed by everyone.

Inspection in Hangzhou: In addition to inspecting Jiaotong University, Mr. Pan has also inspected other universities in Shanghai, such as Guanghua, Jinan, and Tongji. Starting today, he will inspect various middle schools in the city. In a few days, he will leave Shanghai for Hangzhou, where the Hangzhou City autumn military training review for various schools is scheduled to begin on the 12th. Mr. Pan has decided to personally attend for political instruction.

Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter Four: A Cup of Water Reveals the Plight of a Poor Laborer Protecting the Elderly; Ten Thousand Taels Discussed, Cunning Officials Conspire

Zhiqian smiled and said, "You are too kind, old man." He took the earthenware bowl from the old worker's hand and carefully wiped it with a clean piece of paper. Without waiting for the old worker to say anything, he poured the biscuits into the bowl and handed it back, saying, "Don't you like sweet things? These biscuits are very sweet." The old worker took the bowl and said with a smile, "You are too kind to me. I can't refuse. I'll take it back for my daughter." He held the bowl with both hands and bowed twice. Zhiqian smiled and said, "You're too polite. You're making me feel embarrassed." The old worker had nothing to say and smiled at him before leaving. At this moment, a waiter entered the room. Zhiqian thought that since the water in Xiguan was good, the residents would naturally live in the west of the city. He asked the waiter, "Are the houses in Xiguan expensive?" The waiter replied, "Most of the residents live in the west of the city. Does Mr. Cheng want to rent a house? There are too many outsiders coming to Xi'an now, and houses are hard to rent. I can ask someone to inquire for you." Zhiqian said, "I won't be staying in Xi'an for long. What would I rent a house for? I was just asking. I have something else to ask you. Who are the contractors who build houses here? I think that person is quite formidable." The waiter smiled and said, "He used to carry a gun." He lowered his voice and whispered some information. Then he raised his voice and said, "That bricklayer is very pitiful. He's over sixty years old, but he's afraid people will think he's old, so he hasn't dared to grow a beard." Hearing this, Zhiqian sighed twice. He said, "He's so old and still working so hard. He can't even afford a sip of cold water. I feel sorry for him. If I have the chance, I'll help him out. Don't tell him yet." The waiter smiled and said, "You're a good person." Then he whispered, "That girl is also pitiful. You should help her too." Zhiqian smiled and shook his head, saying, "You're wrong. I'm not that kind of person. You want to be a matchmaker." He pointed towards the room next door, and the waiter smiled and walked out. (59)

Son and Wife

— By Yang Yusheng

A son is always good, unconditionally one's own.

Although some say, "A son is the fine that romantic comedy gives you," people are mostly happy to pay this "fine," whether they can afford it or not. If someone is "uniquely blessed" and exempt from paying the "fine," he must create pretexts and exhaust all methods to compete for the "fine," and then be satisfied. Things in this world mostly contain contradictions!

After people compete for this "fine," troubles come endlessly. Production costs, childcare costs, education costs, marriage costs, medical expenses for illnesses, and various other expenses, even if you can afford these economically, the mental pain, just the "parents only worry about their children's illnesses" alone, is enough to trouble and exhaust you. Think about it, people endure all kinds of hardships for their own sons without complaint. Why aren't they like this for other people's sons? This is the genuine "love" in human nature. So, when talking about sons, they are always one's own good ones, even if it inevitably involves a bit of bias, but from the standpoint of love, there is an inner truth that must be said.

A wife is not like this; because the component of genuine love in human nature is much less compared to that of a son. The titles of "same quilt" and "same grave" are certainly grand, but husbands mostly like to find fault with their wives, and their faults gradually reveal themselves over time. Although there is inevitably fault-finding perfectionism, the "dissatisfaction" left in the husband's heart is the source of all divorces—in fact, husbands rarely feel completely satisfied with their wives. So they feel that "other people's wives are better." However, the good qualities of other people's wives are not as unconditional as the good qualities of one's own son, so wives can still use magic to catch up with the good qualities of other people's wives, making their husbands feel satisfied.

Clarification of the Debate on Cattail Shoots and Asparagus

— By Fufu Sheng

After reading Mr. Nanggong Sheng's discussion of Jinan cattail shoots, written in great detail, there are some slight misunderstandings that I would like to correct. Cattail shoots are a section of the cattail root that is submerged in water. The part that emerges from the water is the green leaves of the cattail. Although it is said to be a specialty of Daming Lake, the output is not large. It relies entirely on the production from Zhangyuan outside the city and other places with paddy fields and ponds in the outer counties, which are transported to Jinan for sale throughout the year, continuously from May to October. This is the time of production, and the price is also cheap. The price is highest in January and February, because farmers select the most tender cattail shoots, store them properly, and can therefore get a good price. As for scallion heads and asparagus, that is simply not true. Cattail shoots and asparagus are completely different. Cattail shoots are aquatic plants, like scallions, with a crisp texture. Asparagus are terrestrial plants, like water chestnuts, with a soft texture. When the Germans occupied Qingdao, a German merchant named Rinner brought vegetable seeds and tried planting them in Hongshiya, Haixi. Among them was asparagus. A few months later, fresh asparagus was sold in the Qingdao market for one dollar per pound. After a few years, Rinner's business failed, and vegetable cultivation also stopped. Since then, fresh asparagus has not been seen in the market. If cattail shoots could be made into canned asparagus, Jinan currently has Taikang and Shanghai Food Company, canned food factories, which produce many kinds of products, such as chicken, duck, beef, mutton, vegetables, green beans, and fruits, which are widely sold in various places. How could they not make asparagus? Moreover, no foreign merchants have been seen changing to buy cattail shoots in Jinan. Qingdao Customs has never heard of cattail shoots being exported. From the above, it can be known that asparagus is not a domestic raw material but is entirely imported, which is beyond doubt. Furthermore, it is said that the annual production of Daming Lake cattail shoots in Jinan is always around one million yuan. This statement is even more wrong. The lake surface of several square miles is mainly used for fish ponds and lotus leaves. Cattail shoots are still in the minority. The annual output is more than 20,000 yuan. If it is cattail shoots alone, it will definitely not exceed 3,000 yuan. The so-called total of one million yuan, I don't know where it is calculated from, is hundreds of times different. (Que Chou)
