Remuneration Regulations

The time for issuing remuneration at this publication is from the 6th to the 10th of each month, and again from the 16th to the 20th of each month, except on Sundays, from 2 p.m. to 4 p.m. at the accounting office of this publication. Please prepare a receipt, affix a chop that is the same as the one on the original manuscript, and proceed directly to collect it. If taking the remuneration for several months together, separate receipts with chops must be prepared for each month to facilitate attachment to the ledger. Regarding the chop, whether the article is long or short, or how many times you contribute per month, please affix a chop to each article for verification of the seal when collecting remuneration. If no chop is affixed, it will be considered as a rejection of remuneration. Furthermore, the remuneration period is six months from the date of publication. If it has not been claimed by then, it will be considered that the recipient does not wish to receive the remuneration, and it will be canceled to finalize the account.

Shen Bao Chun Qiu Editorial Department

World Rare News

— (Bingyu)

World's Oldest Age

The world's oldest person was originally a Turk named Sal Argan, who lived to be 135 years old. He could remember the past history within a century and a half. He married three times and had five sons, all of whom died on the battlefield. He suddenly suffered a stroke two years ago and could not get up. However, he had said before his death that he could live to 160 years old. His wife, Ahmed Beiyi, is also 135 years old this year. She is now in good spirits. During the Sevastopol War in 1854, she personally visited the battlefield, so the situation she experienced is still vivid in her mind today.

Largest Camera

This time, a very large camera was found in the basement of the Washington Department of Commerce. It weighed 14 tons and was 30 feet long and wide, like an iron bridge. It was made of 37-inch steel and the base was suspended by iron cables. This huge camera is intended for precise aerial mapping photography. The photographer walks into the machine to take pictures, and can develop the film and process the image inside. It is said that the manufacturing cost is US$15,200, and the assembly took two years of engineering.

Total Amount of Gems

The famous gem merchant, Strong Tu Mide, investigated the total amount of all gems in the world, which is 50 tons, with a market value of 70 billion yuan. There are now 500,000 workers engaged in mining gems in mines around the world, polishers, merchants who pack jewelry rings, more than 25,000, and 100,000 stores selling them. Recently, due to the global economic depression, sales have been declining, but in recent years, the use of gems is not limited to decoration, and gems are also used in industry for drilling.

German News

The German News Research Association released a report for the first half of 1934, publicly listing national news statistics. In total, there were 3,097 daily newspapers in the country, with a circulation of 16,687,595 copies, an average of one copy for every 21,000 people.

World's First Bathing Beach

The Poplar Autonomous Region in London, England, has a population of about 170,000. Recently, a large-scale public bathing beach was built in the area. The various facilities are more elaborate than the world's first Vienna bathhouse. The estimated construction cost is 1.7 million yuan. The building has two large bath halls, 86 slipper-shaped bathtubs, and two squares with concert halls, theaters, and dance halls.

Eighty-Year-Old Bride

About half a century ago, a young man named Charlie Edwardwick fell in love with a woman named Elisa Peps Miceworth. Both were rural people. Because their parents were against their union, they each married other people. Time flies, Charlie's waist is hunched, and Miceworth's face is pale. By coincidence, Miceworth's husband died, and Charlie's wife died. They both recalled their past love and remarried. They officially married at the Aikinx Church last summer, and made a vow to grow old together in the same grave. The groom is now 80 years old, and the bride is 75 years old. The union of this couple is unheard of in the world.

Street Without Tobacco

On a certain day, the tobacco in all the tobacco shops on Gare Street facing the Davia Strait suddenly sold out, and the people in the city who smoked were panicked. This was because the entire French territory was affected by the frozen kiln on a certain day. The road from Gare to Pruneux was also impassable, and the tobacco in Gare City was transported from Pruneux once a week. Coincidentally, the inventory of each tobacco shop in the city was sold out, causing a city-wide tobacco shortage.

The dates are the 9th, 10th, and 11th of this month, a total of three days. Anyone with artistic hobbies is welcome to visit. Yesterday, I received a couplet as a gift, and I hereby acknowledge it.

Ping Jun Jian: Received your letter, I regret that I cannot answer your query about where to purchase red beans. Spring and Autumn General Editorial Department Bai

The Ethereal Record of Imperial Fragrance

— Originally Written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, Translated by Qin Shouou

After a while, she began to speak. This sentence was addressed to Li Lianying.

"Stop the music!"

Although I didn't know why she suddenly wanted to stop the band's performance, I myself found the notes played by this ancient band to be annoyingly noisy. If it were not for the palace customs, I would have long ago used all kinds of methods to persuade the Empress Dowager to disband them.

Because the Empress Dowager had never shown the slightest annoyance with this ancient band, and she also understood a few old tunes. She always ordered the music to stop when a song had ended. But now, she unexpectedly stopped them suddenly, making them The tune they played was abruptly covered up like someone who had been strangled to death. This situation was of course very abnormal. Therefore, the musicians were all flustered and at a loss. They could not put their instruments back on the rack in time, and hurriedly crawled on the ground, kowtowing desperately, fearing that they had unknowingly violated some criminal law, or that there was an error in the tune they played, causing the Empress Dowager to be annoyed.

But the Empress Dowager did not pay attention to them at all, and muttered to herself:

"Today is the first time we have set foot on this piece of land that truly belongs to us; now, we are back! Let us return to our daily life as before!"

What she said was very simple and touching, like intimate words spoken by an emotional person, unlike an order issued by an Empress Dowager; and the daily life indicated in this order was actually just a kind of prison life that strictly followed the palace system passed down for hundreds of years and was boring to death. (169)

Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

Contribution Words

Mr. Hu Wenhu and the National Products Enterprise

— Yang'an

Mr. Hu Wenhu, a prominent overseas Chinese entrepreneur from Southeast Asia, has come north for observation. The people of Shanghai warmly welcome him, with unprecedented enthusiasm. This demonstrates that running a large enterprise, though seemingly impossible, is still very much viable. Our publication welcomes Mr. Hu from the standpoint of the national products industry, as there are significant reasons for doing so:

The state of the national products industry today is extremely bleak. It is constrained at every turn and burdened by heavy taxes. We do not control tariff rights, and the force of dumping is overwhelming. Ordinary factories face financial difficulties, and their operations are plagued by hidden dangers. When they appeal to the government, the government is unable to help. When they seek assistance from banks, the banks are too busy looking after their own interests. Exchange rates rise sharply for no reason, and sales suddenly stagnate. Foreign merchants, as enemies, not only import goods but also establish factories within our borders to seize our livelihoods and control our fate. Small factories are closing down one after another, and large factories are in precarious situations. The markets everywhere are filled with foreign goods or enemy goods. The people have short-sighted views, and many are solely focused on profit. Consequently, the fate of national products is becoming even more pessimistic. Upon observation, how many Chinese-run factories today are successful? It is painful to talk about and saddening to think about.

Mr. Hu possesses great aspirations and boldness. His enterprises, besides the Tiger Balm Yong An Tang, are all dedicated to serving society and benefiting the people. We sincerely hope that after arriving in Shanghai, he will uphold his spirit of serving society and his grand ambition of benefiting the people. He should promote and invest in the national products industry as much as possible. For the nearly dying national products industry, if it is within his power, we hope he will provide assistance and encouragement. It should be noted that the progress of national products today is different from what it was ten years ago, or even five or three years ago. Many exquisite products clearly have the potential to surpass imported goods. When Mr. Hu observes this, he will surely be surprised and realize it is the result of the national products industry's efforts. The China Production and Sales Association, which leads over a hundred factories, and the more than ten China National Products Companies established jointly with comrades in various regions, are especially noteworthy for their enthusiasm, perseverance, and consistent spirit. Mr. Hu should provide them with strong support to facilitate their progress. When he encounters industries that need to be discussed and factories that need to be maintained, Mr. Hu should not hesitate to help them succeed, as the only way to save China is through the national products enterprise. Since Mr. Hu is deeply patriotic, his love for national products must be even more profound. During the enthusiastic welcome given to him by the city, we offer this humble suggestion for his reference. What does Mr. Hu think?

National Products Contributions

Some Small Contributions to the National Products Market

— Yue Xing

Stepping out of a department store that "comprehensively manages global goods" and entering a national products market that specializes in "domestic products," although the "sparkling jewels" of the former cannot compare with the "dazzling array" of the latter, one can still breathe a slight sigh of relief—hoping for its future "daily renewal"!

However, reality will disappoint you even more: the staff's "high and mighty" attitude is no less than those who rely on "foreign brands"; the disharmony between the layout and staff allocation; the lack of meticulousness in handling affairs, etc., can all be found under your scrutiny. Are these things really not necessary or impossible to improve?

Let's first talk about the "staff" aspect:

The staff of a store is crucial to the future of trade; there is no need to elaborate on this. However, the staff of a national products market should especially have a humble and sincere attitude to deal with customers from the "upper-class mansions" to the "low-income apartments," and must never show two different "attitudes" based on people's wealth! But who can guarantee that this situation will not happen? And that it is prevalent! The well-dressed often receive attentive service from the staff, while the honest and simple often face the staff's cold stares, harsh expressions, and neglect. Is this right? Its impact on the future of national products is not insignificant! In the future, I hope that various national products markets will pay more attention to this aspect!

Second, the layout and staff allocation should cater to the psychology of the community.

For example, at a counter selling hats priced at two yuan or a little over one yuan, we can guess that the customers are definitely not gentlemen or young masters, but rather a large group of middle and lower-class brokers (they are the large group in the city and also the main consumers of "broker" hats). Now, having one or two fashionable female staff members supporting this counter will at least violate "their" psychology—or may even make them shy away. (A certain national products market once had the same situation, and as a result, the sales of low-priced goods were extremely poor). Therefore, for low-priced sections, it is best to assign more amiable—or older, more experienced—male staff members, as this would be more appropriate. In addition, the layout of this low-priced goods section should be simple and "practical" in order to easily attract the so-called "middle and lower classes." (We often see that certain foreign low-priced goods can easily penetrate our country's poor classes because they are sold by small shops that do not emphasize luxury).

Third, strive for meticulousness in handling affairs.

When running into any national products market, one often encounters the situation where staff cannot answer the price—or sometimes say a little more or a little less. This is due to the staff's indifference to trade! As for the staff's slow movements (such as arbitrarily chatting with people while the packaging is not completed), casual laughter, and listlessness—the most abominable is that when customers inquire, the staff often reply with the words: "National products are inherently not excellent," "National products are only like this," or falsely claim that the goods are good in order to deceive customers. All of this causes customers to have extremely unpleasant feelings and, as a result, distrust national products. What is the extent of the harm caused by this! Those who run national products businesses should pay attention to this! And there should be adequate training and guidance to these staff members in order to improve their skills.

Today, when foreign goods are dumped and the future of domestic products is bleak, although the above points are minor, many people are dissatisfied with and despise national products markets because of them. I hope that those who run domestic products businesses will not overlook them by "focusing on the small details"!

National Products Discussion

Deliberations on Trademarks

— Zhu Jianhua

In these years when everyone is promoting national products, commodity trademarks are indeed very important. For example, the recent trademark exhibition held in Hangzhou displayed various trademarks of domestic and foreign goods, classified and listed side by side, in the hope that the general public would have something to follow when purchasing national products. The depth of this intention and the importance of trademarks in national products can be imagined.

Let's try to discuss this issue in three layers: First, is the use of English in trademarks (mostly English) due to the misconception that Chinese people have a psychology of worshiping foreign things and therefore apply it to domestic products? I believe that "true gold fears no fire," why must we rely on foreign words for trademarks? This can be clearly demonstrated by taking the most famous domestic product manufacturers as examples, such as Kang Yuan Canning Factory, Zhanghua Woolen Mill...etc. Their products are far superior to imported goods. The exclusive use of Chinese characters in a certain country's trademarks at the Hangzhou Exhibition is enough to make us deeply appreciate this. Especially for domestic cosmetics, nineteen out of ten use English decoration, and some even use all English. The general public who intend to buy domestic products but do not understand English all think that they are not domestic products and want to buy them but stop. This is not a false statement, it is indeed what I and many friends have personally experienced. Therefore, in my opinion, domestic products should all use Chinese, and clearly indicating the manufacturer is especially important.

The second issue is "name." I believe that the name of a trademark should be elegant and appreciated by all, known to both the old and the young, and easy to remember. For example, the cigarette trademarks of a certain foreign cigarette company all cater to our national conditions. Some even use the most common and familiar place names as trademarks, which shows how far-sighted they are. However, our domestic product trademarks mostly use foreign names, terms, and Europeanized names, which is really too much to cater to the general public's psychology and even forget our ancestors.

The third is the homophony of names. There has been a lot of controversy over the homophony of trademark names before, which is a very painful thing. It should be known that in this era when our country's industry and commerce have not yet flourished, it is appropriate for everyone to work together with one heart, each with their own responsibilities, to fight against foreign goods and seek a way out. How can we aim to profit for ourselves and promote our own products by borrowing the homophony of other people's well-known trademarks? As long as our own products are excellent and promoted properly, there is no way that they cannot be developed and sold widely in various places.

Finally, I would like to put forward a very small but very important matter, that is, please all domestic product manufacturers unite to create a common hidden mark and print it on each product. The simpler, clearer, and more suitable size is the best. In this way, for those who intend to buy domestic products, there will be a definite and unswerving target. The promotion is easy, and the effect is great. Why not do it?

National Products Talk

Can I Do It Well Alone?

— Ba Ling

I often chat with friends and talk about national products issues: Among them, three friends said very negatively: "Promoting national products is of course our obligation, but is it useful for me to do it alone? Although I personally try my best to use national products and desperately purchase national products, most people in society are not aware and still buy foreign goods, so what's the use of me alone?..." On the surface, this friend's tone seems to be correct, as if there is a considerable reason, but upon careful thought, it is extremely wrong and completely absurd.

Why is this friend's tone wrong and absurd? Because we must know and deeply understand that society is a collection of individuals. Many, many individuals "gather together to create a society, so the individual is the starting point of society and also the backbone of society. It is certainly a good phenomenon that every individual in society becomes aware together, and everyone vows to use national products. Even if a large portion of individuals faithfully use national products and gradually influence others, this is not necessarily a good national products promotion method. Therefore, we cannot despise the individual and say something like 'What's the use of me promoting national products alone?' You must know that from me personally promoting national products, setting an example, and earnestly implementing it, and from me influencing my family, my relatives, and my friends, the effect is really very great! How can we say such unreasonable words?"

Therefore, here, I want to offer an opinion to friends who are enthusiastically promoting national products. When we encounter this kind of friend, we can say to this person with a gentle expression: "As long as you rely on yourself alone, you will definitely do it well. You must value yourself and respect yourself. You see, several prosperous national products factories are so developed because they rely on one of them in the factory, rely on that person alone, and they do it well. Of course, you can do it well too. Don't be discouraged, hurry up and work hard!" If we use these words to deal with others and patiently persuade them, they will definitely be moved, they will definitely correct their wrong ideas, and they will become active. Therefore, "Can I do it well alone?" This sentence, we should overthrow it.

National Products Photo

Comparison of Foreign Goods Import Surplus

— Shan

Dear compatriots, quickly switch to using national products! Don't hesitate, economic subjugation is imminent.

I will now write down the annual accounts of international trade import surplus—I hope that compatriots will carefully observe them to be alarmed.

1930—More than 414.9 million taels.

1931—More than 540 million taels. Compared with the two years, the year increased by more than 125 million taels.

1932—Imports exceeded exports by 556.60524 million customs taels; this year increased by more than 325.9 million customs taels compared with 1931.

1933—Imports of foreign goods totaled about 130 million yuan, while exports were only about 60 million yuan; from this point of view, imports exceeded exports by as much as 70 million yuan. Isn't it shocking?

Looking at the trade every year, the import surplus of foreign goods increases year by year; if this continues, won't the economy be subjugated? This kind of subjugation is truly unknown to gods and ghosts. Dear compatriots! Wake up quickly! Don't be anesthetized by foreign goods! Aren't you afraid? But this kind of subjugation is even more terrible than the planes and cannons of the Japanese devils.

Dear compatriots! Quickly go to the national products market to diagnose your anesthetic disease! Don't live your leisurely life in a careless way! If you don't wake up again, the country will soon be destroyed in your hands.

The Past and Present of the Shanghai Rosewood Furniture Industry

— He Gongxing

An Unbearable Look Back at Bygone Days

In Shanghai's rosewood furniture industry, there are over a hundred businesses, large and small. However, the turnover for the past ten months is only worth over 600,000 yuan, a sight unseen in the last forty years. Rosewood furniture is, after all, a luxury item, and with the decline of people's livelihoods, it's naturally difficult to sell well. In the recent decade, Westerners and Japanese have been quite fond of it. In 1930, rosewood furniture shipped to Japan was worth over 1.2 million yuan, while that to Europe and America was worth about 5-600,000 yuan. By 1931, exports to Japan remained largely unchanged, but those to the West were only worth over 100,000 yuan. By 1932, exports to Japan were less than 30,000 yuan, and those to the West had also dropped to around 10,000 yuan. This year, neither Japanese nor Western firms have made any purchases. Occasionally, there are only small, scattered pieces. Inquiries to stores like Qiaoyuantai and Tao Yongren can give an idea of the overall situation.

The most prosperous era for the rosewood furniture industry was during the late Qing Dynasty. Opium dens and gambling houses were the main customers at the time. After 1924, items such as zither tables, nesting tables, dragon head stands, clock stands (for hanging round copper mirrors), snuffboxes, writing trays, canes, etc., were all favored by Europeans and Americans, especially Americans, who were particularly fond of them. For clock stands alone, each export batch was always around 2-30,000 pieces. Later, a trend of devaluation and competitive selling emerged. Coupled with the fact that unemployed workers purchased small pieces of lumber and manufactured them at home, standing at the doors of foreign firms and peddling them to foreigners at low prices, items that used to cost over three yuan each now sold for only two yuan, or even one yuan each. Foreigners competed to buy them, and as sales increased, so did the number of manufacturers, and prices continued to fall, while the quality of goods deteriorated further and further. Ultimately, they were rejected by foreigners, which was a major cause of their failure. Also, the rise of Western-style furniture, the emergence of the steel furniture industry, and the popularity of iron beds led to the gradual decline of the rosewood furniture industry.

The Shanghai rosewood furniture industry is divided into two categories: one is the rosewood dowry industry, specializing in large rosewood furniture; the other is the rosewood small pieces industry, specializing in various small rosewood items. It's entirely handicraft-based, and traditionally dominated by people from Yangzhou. In the past twenty years, people from Menghe, Jiangyin, have risen to replace them. Internally, the industry has polishing workshops and lacquering workshops, but no woodworking workshops. This is because the manufacturing of rosewood furniture is outsourced to the white wood body industry. The rosewood furniture industry orders from the white wood body industry, then polishes and lacquers them for sale. The polishing work is particularly important to the industry. The price of the same item can vary greatly, often depending on the quality of the polishing. China's manufacturing of rosewood furniture began in the Ming Dynasty. The wood initially came from Annam, but recently, it's mostly imported from Siam. The price is measured by weight, around 18 yuan per dan (a unit of weight). In recent years, rosewood and fragrant rosewood have also come from Siam, but their quality and texture are inferior, and the price is also lower. However, since the prevalence of Western-style modern furniture, rosewood furniture manufacturers, in order to cater to the psychology of buyers, often inlay the surface of rosewood furniture with burl wood patterns to enhance its beauty. The burl wood is often mistaken for decayed wood, but burl wood is burl wood, and decayed wood is decayed wood. The business of trading these wood materials is the rosewood disassembly industry.

Page 18

Free Talk

On the Lives of Literati During the Wei and Jin Dynasties

— Cao Juren

In those two hundred years from the first year of Zhongping during the reign of Emperor Ling of the Han Dynasty (when the Yellow Turban Rebellion began) to the first year of Yuanxi during the reign of Emperor Gong of the Eastern Jin Dynasty (when the Jin Dynasty fell), the death of a person or two was not something to be concerned about. As early as the reign of Emperor Huan of the Han Dynasty, "the dead in the capital were piled upon each other, and in the counties, they were everywhere in the fields." By the early Eastern Jin Dynasty, "the Central Plains were desolate, with no smoke for a thousand miles; the hungry and cold wandered and fell into ditches one after another." "Yanling used to have fifty to sixty thousand households, but now there are only a few hundred." What a great Asura field this was! But historians did not seem very concerned about the life and death of these people. The deaths of a few literati were written about in great detail, leaving a deep impression on later generations. The practice of the authorities executing literati began with Huang Zu killing Mi Heng. Cao Cao followed suit and killed the talkative Kong Rong. Cao Pi also killed many literati, and if it weren't for the brotherly love, even Cao Zhi would have almost been unable to escape. (In fact, brotherly love didn't matter much to Cao Pi: the Prince of Rencheng was killed by Cao Pi.) At the end of the Three Kingdoms period, those famous scholars, Sima Yi, killed two—Xiahou Xuan and He Yan, and Sima Zhao also killed one—Ji Kang. Their crimes were roughly the same: unfilial piety. However, Zang Rongxu said in the Biography of Ruan Ji in the Book of Jin: "During the transition from the Wei to the Jin Dynasty, the world was full of disasters, and few famous scholars survived. Therefore, Ruan Ji did not engage in worldly affairs and became addicted to drinking. ... Zhong Hui asked him about current affairs several times, wanting to use his approval or disapproval to accuse him, but he always escaped because of his drunkenness." This is the truth. We all know that Cao Cao, Cao Pi, Sima Yi, and Sima Zhao were not loyal ministers or filial sons themselves; using "unfilial piety" to kill those famous scholars was just a pretext.

Someone might ask Cao Cao and Sima Yi: Why did you have to execute literati? Let's first talk about a few foreign stories: Why couldn't the Greeks, a nation that prided itself on freedom, allow the great philosopher Socrates to live a few more years? Socrates was already seventy-one years old when he died, and he would have died sooner or later; the Greeks were in such a hurry to get rid of this person. Socrates did not commit any major crimes; he only questioned people, arousing young people's doubts about the status quo and preventing the Greeks from continuing to live in a drunken dream. Therefore, the three people who accused him, Meletus, etc., said that he "denied the gods recognized by the state, sang of new gods, and corrupted the youth of Athens." This is one thing. Another thing happened during the French Revolution, a figure we Chinese are most familiar with: Madame Roland. When she was about to die, she said to the statue of the goddess of liberty: "Liberty! Liberty! How many crimes have people committed in your beautiful name!" Her husband committed suicide the same day after hearing the news of her murder; he left a small note, saying: "I hope that the whole country will abandon this heinous crime of killing the innocent and turn around to discover true humanity!" Both she and her husband had the habit of lecturing others, and they never realized it until they died! The literati of the Wei and Jin dynasties probably suffered from the same problem of being talkative, and they had to express a long and short reason for everything, even reciting the Classic of Filial Piety to the Yellow Turbans; "It's impossible to reason with soldiers," who would bother listening to your nagging? When we read Ji Kang's letter to Shan Juyuan, we find it ridiculous: what "seven unbearables," what "two impossibilities," only cause headaches, and thus send him to the guillotine. Even the so-called pastoral poet Tao Yuanming could not avoid this problem (such as Miscellaneous Poems, Imitating the Ancients, and Reading the Classic of Mountains and Seas, there is anger and resentment in every word); let alone other literati. Under certain circumstances, it can be said that the unfortunate ending of literati is destined!

Their method of escaping reality seems quite humorous to us. Among them, three ancient books were popular: Laozi, Zhuangzi, and the Book of Changes. Laozi and Zhuangzi both taught people to return to a state of chaos where there is no right and wrong and no difference: "Never taking the lead, but always following others; everyone takes reality, but he alone takes emptiness; everyone seeks happiness, but he alone seeks completion." If people don't know that the human heart is like a mirror, once it reaches a state of emptiness and stillness, even secrets can be seen clearly: it is better to muddle along in the world of profit and power, truly able to be in darkness, not seeing the light of day. In this way, they wanted to find a hiding place in Lao-Zhuang philosophy to settle down, but as a result, they saw right and wrong more clearly and were even less able to settle down. Their second method of escaping reality was drinking. When Sima Zhao wanted to propose marriage to Ruan Ji on behalf of Sima Shi, Ruan Ji was drunk for sixty days, making it impossible for the envoy to open his mouth. Escaping by drunkenness was only effective this one time. Later, when Sima Yan let go of the Nine Bestowments, the dukes and ministers wanted to urge him to advance. Ruan Ji was ordered to write the persuasion, whether or not he wanted to. Ruan Ji also wanted to escape by drunkenness, but it was impossible after all; he had to write it on the spot and let the envoy copy it. Ji Kang probably didn't approve of Ruan Ji's method, so he said: "Ruan Sizong; only drinks excessively; until he is bound by the scholars of etiquette, hating him like an enemy..." Because people like Ji Kang would become silent when drunk; Ruan Sizong was originally "harmless to things," but after drinking, he would become abnormal and cause trouble. The third method of escaping reality was to enter the mountains to cultivate the Tao and learn to become immortals. But the more effort one put into cultivating the Tao, the more venomous one became. Sun Deng, who was hidden in Su Men Mountain, bluntly said that Ji Kang "had much talent but little knowledge and would not end well"; fortunately, Ji Kang was not a person who wanted to serve the ruler, otherwise Sun Deng himself would not have ended well. All the methods of self-anesthetization and escape used by the literati of the Wei and Jin dynasties were ineffective, and they could only be like ostriches, burying their heads in the trees, thinking that they had hidden themselves, letting the hunters catch them and slaughter them.

After the Eastern Jin Dynasty, Buddhist thought spread, and the teachings of Shakyamuni replaced the teachings of Laozi and Zhuangzi. The most intelligent people all became monks; they had great things to do in another world and did not have to mix with reality, which was true escape. Moreover, in another world, everything in the human world would be fairly and justly reckoned from scratch, and all the anger and resentment would naturally subside. Therefore, to escape reality, it is difficult to be effective by relying on self-anesthetization alone. The most important thing is to be able to have another universe to go to, like the Buddhists. That would be relatively safe.

Untitled One

— Lin Xi

Crows fly over the roof, roosters crow back and forth, even the donkey gazes at the dawn and whines. Night only leaves sparse black spots.

Looking out the window: fields reveal faint paths, morning wind is already seen atop the sorghum, and an old man's cough comes from the thatched hut.

Isn't it dawn yet? Is it dawn? But before me are cold iron bars! I lower my head, then raise it again, emptily gazing at the distant mountains!

Autumn Love

— Lao Yi

It seems someone once said: spring is like a "lover," while autumn is like a "beloved." That is to say, while the liveliness of spring is certainly lovely, the depth of autumn is especially lovable!

I have never been someone who loved spring much; but I truly love autumn. Just as I usually don't love Li Bai when reading poetry, but love Du Fu, and don't love Maupassant when reading novels, but love Turgenev, it's the same feeling.

Often, I feel, feel the idle thoughts in a guest house, the courtyard at dusk, the phoenix trees in the courtyard, the evening breeze on the phoenix tree leaves, the endless desolate melody coming from the evening breeze! It feels that life is just like this scene.

Plus, the lonely railings, the faint autumn water outside the railings, the fishing boats on the water, the evening songs of the fishermen, the evening songs echoing the distant mountain village, the faint shadows of smoke lingering in the mountain village, a few yellow leaves and red maples locked in the shadows of smoke, the sound of the wind gradually presenting a kind of mournful color! Waves of returning birds, waves of barking dogs, waves of the noisy sound of aggrieved women's laundry mallets, this universe, this life, all of this, you can fully savor! Fully chew! When you chew, you will know, know that the universe is inside, life is inside, everything is inside.

Life is only a few decades. People who have passed thirty already feel that half a lifetime has passed, like the sun that has set to the west: gradually passing, gradually declining. Just like in the middle of the four seasons of the year, if autumn passes, the appearance of all things will be aging day by day, decaying day by day! Can you not feel sad?

People over thirty have tasted all the flavors of the world, and autumn, in the seasons, can be considered to have experienced many misfortunes; therefore, life at thirty makes people nostalgic; autumn in the year is even more nostalgic!

Now, late autumn is coming to an end, and the season is slowly approaching winter. I am already thirty-one years old. I am reluctant to part with autumn, I am reluctant to part with the age of thirty, I deeply feel that autumn is gone, but it will come again; what is there after the age of thirty is gone?

The Ulaqi Desert (Part 1)

— Shi Dai

When the sun came out, a group of people drove livestock from the Nukutai Plain into the Ulaqi Desert.

The Ulaqi Desert is like a calm sea, flat and boundless. The night's wind had long stopped, and the sky was clear without clouds. The sunlight gradually radiated heat. People, camels, horses, cattle, sheep... a dark mass, began to wriggle, the winding line like a long snake. Treading forward.

Bagu Like, riding on a camel, whose usual full of spirit has completely disappeared, hangs his head, wondering what he is thinking? His daughter, Tanila, hit the butt of the camel he was riding with a whip.

—Dad! Can Dali Gangai be reached today?

He raised his head, glanced at his daughter, didn't say anything, squinted his eyes, lowered his head again, and simply closed his eyes.

—Dali Gangai of Heaven ah!

Hope climbed like an ant on everyone's heart, a heat from the depths of the heart, exciting the blood of the whole body, wild imagination in everyone's mind.

The hotter it got, the sun beat the desert hotly, beat people, beat livestock, beat this group of columns, everything was suppressed by the heat. People were sweating profusely, the women's upper clothes were soaked in sweat, tightly clinging to the flesh, and the breasts were clearly visible under the halter. The horse's mouth foamed white. The sheep jumped and bleated. The dog dragged its tongue and panted, running for a while and resting for a while. The camels and cattle were soaked in sweat all over their bodies, shining in the sun.

People's breathing, children's crying, old women's complaints, sheep's wailing, the sound of livestock hooves, ... all kinds of different sounds mixed in the sultry air and swelled up.

They were silent, looking with eyes that hid hope and joy, at the sea-like, flat, vast desert that was connected to the sky.

No one can stop the thoughts, Dali Gangai Heaven is always jumping in the brain, jumping non-stop.

...Dali Gangai, where there are palaces, pavilions, houses, rice to eat, winter without snow, without wind, always warm, the grass is always lush no matter when; this is what the Lama requested of the heavenly gods by the order of Bayan Khan. The gods loved us so much that they gave us this beautiful paradise—Dali Gangai...—When Bayan Khan's envoy, Noyin, announced this news to everyone, who did not envy it? When Bayan Khan then ordered Noyin to lead everyone from the Nukutai Plain to Dali Gangai, everyone was so happy that they jumped up and down. Now they are savoring Noyin's words, hope has become a beautiful flower, spraying sweetness and fragrance in everyone's heart.

Wanderer (1)

— Lu Fen

A dark August afternoon sky.

After the engine roared the first time, the switchman spat out a monotonous phlegm, tapping his leg with a green flag, and slowly walked towards the gate. The quiet little station was suddenly bustling. Cold food vendors, cigarette sellers, children and women selling boiled water... looked towards the smoky distance, waiting for passenger train number eighty-two.

The short old man squatted down, as if he didn't hear those sounds. At the entrance to the station platform, he spread out his satchel as usual. A station attendant in uniform brushed past him and suddenly slapped him on the shoulder.

"Friend, estimate half a catty of white shochu. This time, I won't be stingy."

Saying that, he ran in.

"Oh? Okay, okay... naturally."

Even though he responded, he didn't lift his head.

There was a lot of ash on his beard. Even in August, large beads of sweat oozed from under his somewhat crooked nose. The two buttons of his collar were undone, revealing his purplish-brown collarbones. A felt hat covered his round head, so tattered it looked like a lotus leaf; the brim hung straight down, covering his unusually wide jawbones. No matter how you looked at his haggard appearance, he would never look more like a weary traveler.

Those passengers, mostly belonging to villagers or small merchants, were not noble. Dragging their muddy feet, carrying their tattered luggage, they exhaled a big breath of dark air, wiped their faces covered in coal cinders, and walked lazily out of the entrance.

"Nanhai Guanyin Incense Wafer, (Note) whether paralysis or injury, all kinds of diseases, incurable for years... Are there old people and young children at home?... Three packs are good, five will get rid of the root."

He solicited business in the accent of the Huai River basin; repeatedly muttering, his voice low and lazy. Proving that he was an unadulterated drunkard.

He clearly understood the passengers' weakness: they had toiled for half a year or several years in foreign lands, accumulated some money in their hands, and wanted to go home to see their elderly parents and hardworking wives. Because of poverty, illness would quietly invade their bodies. Only these people had futile filial piety. Going to the hospital to hire a doctor? Unable to. Herbalists also rarely went to the countryside year-round. In order to fulfill their human responsibilities, the young and middle-aged would spend a few dollars. So he squinted his eyes slyly, and his schemes were aimed at this void.

Local Supplement of Shen Bao

Small Talk

Yi Peiji's Stolen Goods

— Wan

Yesterday, I was sitting in my garret when I heard an old woman next door scolding someone. I didn't understand most of it, but I clearly heard her say, "You little rascal, your sins are overflowing, one day you'll walk right into the net." This reminded me of Zheng Zhuang Gong's saying, "Those who commit many unrighteous acts will surely destroy themselves," and Confucius's saying, "Goods that enter improperly will also leave improperly." This is just the way of heaven and earth. The more I thought about the old woman's words, the more sense they made.

Later, I thought about it again, and the old woman's words were an absolutely deterministic view, which is somewhat wrong in the current trend. Now we advocate the theory of human rights and the theory of utilitarianism (forgive my misunderstanding of these two theories). Humans can definitely conquer heaven, and humans should conquer nature. Whoever is strong, who goes to occupy. Whoever has power, who gets to seize territory and snatch jobs. What is called benevolence, righteousness, morality? What is called abiding by the law? These are mostly arguments used by the strong to deceive the weak.

Yi Peiji served as the director of the National Palace Museum in 1929, and Li Zongtong served as the secretary-general. They successively stole parts of the jewelry in their custody, including 1,319 pearls, 526 gems, and replaced 9,606 real pearls with fake pearls, and 3,251 real gems with fake gems. In addition, they disassembled jewelry accessories from 1,496 original items. They also stole entire items, such as silk tassel made of rice pearls and jadeite flower inlaid with jeweled bracelets. The amount was huge, all of which they appropriated for themselves. There were many other cases of encroachment, forgery, and obstruction of official duties, which cannot all be listed.

Now the prosecutor of the Jiangning District Court has completed the investigation and filed a lawsuit. A person like this who steals from himself is guilty of heinous crimes and should be immediately arrested and brought to justice for interrogation. However, Yi Peiji uses the concession as a protector and traitors as a guarantee. It is feared that it will not be easy to arrest him, just like "a robber falling into the sea," where to catch him. He can live a life of leisure outside the law, and spend his days as a parasite in the concession, living a life of ease and wealth.

According to a telegram from Tianjin yesterday: Yi Peiji is hiding on Langsu Street in the Japanese concession of Tianjin, and is extremely unfree. Hoodlums and thugs extort him every day. Zheng Xiaoxu, the rebel, believes that the treasures of the Qing imperial family should belong to the Qing imperial family. He previously sent Japanese An Tianshida, a pseudo-State Council affairs official, to Tianjin to demand most of the treasures from Yi Peiji. Yi was extremely resentful because of this. If that were really the case, then Yi Peiji's petty theft was all in vain, benefiting others. Even I feel a little resentful for him when I think about it.

Then I thought again about the old woman next door's words, "Little rascal, your sins are overflowing, one day you'll walk right into the net." Although the day when sins are overflowing and walking into the net has not yet arrived, that day will always come. Now I see that there are many people like Yi Peiji. Let's take Yi Peiji as an example and ask everyone to take a look.

Cleverness

— Dan Ran

"Cleverness" is of course two good words. Ever since we understood the words of the human world, we have often hoped to be "clever." In particular, parents' desire for their children to be clever can be said to be an almost universal sentiment. However, Su Dongpo said: "Everyone wants their son to be clever, but I have been misled by cleverness all my life. I only hope that my son will be foolish and stupid, and live carefree until he becomes a high official." Many people say that Su Dongpo was a talented scholar, and talented scholars must be clever, but he insisted on saying "I have been misled by cleverness all my life." Then the value of the two words cleverness is a bit doubtful. I know that clever people can certainly say: "Su Dongpo was just clever in reading and writing articles, not clever in penetrating the ways of the world. No wonder he couldn't be a good official and was eventually exiled to death." From general opinion, we can easily find the concept of the two words "cleverness," which is "penetrating the ways of the world, and being adaptable."

However, Confucius had a further analysis. He said: "Great wisdom is like foolishness." From this sentence, we can find two key points: First, wisdom is cleverness. Since there is great cleverness, there is naturally petty cleverness. Then the cleverness mentioned earlier is of course petty cleverness. Second, since great cleverness is somewhat like foolishness, it is naturally difficult for ordinary people to see it. Like Columbus going to the boundless ocean to find land, Watt seeing the pot lid being lifted by boiling water were all considered rare and strange. Before the New World was discovered and the steam engine was invented, clever people would laugh their heads off at the foolishness of Columbus and Watt.

Again, Confucius also said: "Only the highest wisdom and the lowest stupidity are immutable." We can also know that since people with great cleverness and stupid people are both somewhat stubborn, their unsuitability to the times is evident. We can know even more that petty clever people are always "changing allegiances." It is natural for them to be opportunistic and hopeful of advancement.

The Chinese are uniquely blessed, and there are indeed many clever people. There are also a considerable number of people who are not clever but pretend to be clever, but unfortunately, they are all petty clever, with more than enough adaptability and not enough stubbornness. Therefore, the country, society, and even the literary world are in a mess.

Third Sister

— Village Cause

Yesterday; the sunshine was very bright, fresh!

Third Sister returned yesterday, bringing her young daughter.

When she came back, she said to me with surprise:

"Ah! You've grown so tall! It's only been a little over two years since we last met."

A little over two years since we met, Third Sister already had a daughter, and she had aged!

I didn't dare to stir her sorrow, so I only said:

"Time really flies!"

(What season was it, I can't remember! At that time, it was when the pomegranates were in bloom.

—Third Sister! When are you getting married? Soon! Haha.

Those who ran into her always joked with her.

One day, Mom took out a new dress that I had worn once from the trunk for me.

—Cause, tomorrow is the day Third Sister is getting married, you have to go to the wedding!

The next day, I watched her being carried away in a bridal sedan!

I also watched Third Sister's mother, with tears in her smiling face, saying as Third Sister was about to get into the sedan:

—Third Sister! You must take care of yourself!

I heard this sentence very clearly: like the crow's caw in the early morning.

After that:

In the first year, Third Sister did not come back. The news came:

She gave birth to a baby girl.

In the second year, Third Sister did not come back. The news came:

—Her husband fell to his death!

In the third year, Third Sister came back! She brought a story:

—...My husband was a plasterer, his temperament was very gentle, I was married to him for over a year, and we never argued once! Poor him, he fell from a very high five-story building. Dead! God! This western-style building... is a monster! It, it swallowed my husband alive....

Third Sister returned yesterday, bringing her young daughter.

—Third Sister! Are you having a good time in Shanghai?

Speaking of Shanghai, she would become sad and say:

—Shanghai is an execution ground! Sinful, heartbreaking...

Her face resembled that of a lost companion goose: haggard and melancholic.

—Third Sister's fate is not good!

The Third Sister of two or three years ago, was beautiful!

The Third Sister before my eyes is like a withered branch.

—She is only twenty-one years old!

(Poor, young widow! Your life is simple.

The fine-looking chastity arch stands erect, smiling insincerely, saying:

—Come! Third Sister! Join us!)

Yesterday, the sunshine was very bright, fresh!

(It was the day Third Sister returned.)

Today, it is raining continuously. Washing everything on this earth.

Tomorrow, the day after tomorrow... let's wait and see! However, Third Sister always curses those tall western-style buildings.

Anemia

— Yu Renying

Two children, silently; jostling on the public bus. A bunch of fresh flowers, a basket of apples.

The bus turned onto a quiet road. The low western-style houses on both sides, inside, wallpapered with Parisian floral paper, could be seen through the bus windows; fleshy White Russian women were applying lipstick.

Getting off the bus, groping on the unfamiliar road. The five characters "×× Sanatorium" jumped into our eyes, asked the doorman.

"Where is the first-class ward?" Found the third floor, bumped into a white-clad angel in the corridor.

"Which room is Miss Wang ×× in?" She asked me for a calling card, we waited at the doorway. After she came out,

"Can we go in?" She nodded. White powder walls, white iron bed, white bedding...; facing a sunny window.

"Who told you I was here?" I gave a knowing smile.

"Anemia, this popular disease!" Her face was indeed much thinner, just last week I saw her knitting a wool sweater at home.

"Is the environment here good?"

"Good enough. I go to the garden for a sunbath every day. Now I can only eat things like cod liver oil, fruit, and eggs."

Sitting by the south-facing window, watching the dwarf holly garden path, white-clad angels, white-clad patients; breathing in the faint sunlight of the Mid-Autumn Festival.

"I'll come see you again on National Day, I hope you recover soon." We shook hands tightly. Jumping on the number nine public bus, the carriage was quiet.

The torrent of the city, makes everyone fall into the death line of anemia. Facing the lonely street scene, deeply sighing.

Thinking of one's own situation struggling for life while sick; a paradise for the bourgeoisie to recuperate flashed before my eyes again.

Amateur Mailbox

A New Method of Buying National Products

Editor:

Chinese science is undeveloped, industry and commerce lag behind others, and various products are rarely improved, so most are not as good as others. Generally, people naturally want to use a better item, so those foreign goods are happily used by Chinese people. But I don't think Chinese people necessarily have to buy foreign goods. If domestic goods can improve, and clerks can pay attention to promoting domestic goods, and try to introduce the benefits of domestic goods to them, then they will also change their habit of buying foreign goods. Speaking of this, some clerks must say: "Promoting domestic goods is the responsibility of the government, industrialists, shop owners, and all customers. We clerks are just doing what we are told, without any freedom to exercise our will. Where would there be an opportunity to promote domestic goods? And if we did work outside of our duties, then there is always the risk of losing our jobs!" This statement, on the surface, seems to have considerable reason, but based on my few years of experience, when actually studied, it is not necessarily so. I feel that it is very suitable to promote domestic goods from the position of a clerk, and there are many convenient places. Now I am writing my experience below, hoping that clerks and other readers will have a thorough discussion.

I am also a clerk in a store. This store has been open for several years. It is a department store, and most of the goods in the store are foreign goods, among which Japanese goods account for the largest number. Because Japanese goods are cheap and look very beautiful on the surface, although when used,

Page 21

they are not durable, but the psychology of our Chinese people is to only seek immediate benefits, and have no time to consider what will happen in the future. Therefore, Japanese goods sell very well, and the store owner also takes as much in as possible because it is profitable. A long time ago, we clerks wanted to ask the boss to import less foreign goods and promote domestic goods more, in order to recover our rights and interests, but we felt that this was not the boss's problem but the customer's problem. If all customers came to buy domestic goods, then foreign goods would naturally be eliminated, and the boss would naturally stop importing foreign goods. If we forced the boss not to import foreign goods, wouldn't this store have to close? So we also thought of the method of persuading customers. But three years ago, Japan's ferocious face had not yet appeared, and the Chinese people had not yet realized the terrible nature of the military and economic aggression of various countries, and because of the habit of using foreign goods and the psychology of being greedy for cheapness, although we advised them, or her, to buy domestic goods, the result was rarely effective, especially their or her attitude of despising domestic goods, which made people feel very disappointed.

Later, the September 18th Incident occurred, and Japan's military aggression aroused the patriotic enthusiasm of the Chinese people, and they were a little hostile to Japanese goods, so our best opportunity to promote domestic goods came.

When customers just ran into the store, we clerks would talk to him about the abominableness of Japan, and the losses of China, and also talk about the benefits of buying domestic goods. If he was knowledgeable, he would definitely not buy Japanese goods or other foreign goods, and for the sake of face, he would be embarrassed to buy foreign goods again. If that customer was a truly uneducated person with no patriotism, completely didn't understand what we said, and insisted on buying Japanese goods, then we also had a way to deal with it. For example, if he wanted to buy a pair of Japanese rubber shoes, we would show them to him as usual, but always take those more worn-out goods, and say to them, Japan is not paying attention to industry and commerce because they are preparing for war, so their goods are not as good as before. At the same time, take a pair of newly arrived domestic goods and show them to him. Although they are used to seeing Japanese goods, if they see that Japanese goods are not as good as domestic goods, then they will also change to buying domestic goods. As for those who buy foreign goods, we also use the same method to deal with them, and the result is very good. It can be seen that Chinese people don't necessarily have to buy foreign goods. As long as clerks can pay attention to this point, I think the future of domestic goods will be relatively promising.

This kind of method of promoting domestic goods does not cause any loss to the boss, because his purpose of opening a store is just to make money. If domestic goods can sell well, he can also make money, he will definitely not be willing to promote foreign goods and be a "traitorous merchant" and be scolded by the Chinese people. Apricot Light Above

Novel

Liu Desheng in Jiangxi

— Wan Guoan

(1) The crutch is gone

After climbing over one mountain, there was another one right after it. Mountains were everywhere, left, right, front, and back. Liu Desheng became more and more anxious as he climbed! The rifle he was holding in his hand had simply turned into his crutch. This big black guy undoubtedly forgot his mission as a scout, and kept using all his strength to climb forward.

The two scouts who had set off with him on his right were now nowhere to be seen. After climbing forward for several dozen meters, he would hold onto the small trees on the hillside, open his big mouth revealing a pair of tiger teeth, and gasp for breath.

"Damn it! That's just messing around, where did these bandits come from, making me climb mountains like this, you could climb yourself to death and not see one." After the big black guy had almost caught his breath, he cursed like this while climbing forward again.

The weather in southern Jiangxi in July was already particularly hot. Although a cool breeze was blowing from the mountain tops from time to time, the scorching sun made oil pour from the forehead of this big black ant-like Liu Desheng.

"I'm not doing it anymore! Damn it, not doing it again!"

This big black guy really couldn't take it anymore! He plopped down onto the weeds, and if it wasn't for the small tree next to him blocking him, he would have almost rolled down.

"Moved your maternal uncle's!"

The big black guy's explosive temper erupted, and he reached out to throw the gun away.

"Little maternal uncle! If it wasn't for you being my crutch, I would have really thrown you away in this Jiangxi mountain."

This was the big black guy sitting on the grass, breathing heavily and slowly with his mouth, staring blankly at the clear sky with his big eyes, forgetting everything, and only caring about savoring this comfortable feeling of reality. The more he sat, the more he liked it, and his eyes gradually closed together. "Taking a nap" after great fatigue is so precious!

Sinology

Miss Bingmei's Selected Tang Poems

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Song of Everlasting Regret (Continued)

A Taoist from Linqiong, a guest from the Phoenix Capital, Able to reach the soul with sincerity. Moved by the monarch's lingering thoughts, He ordered the Taoist priest to diligently seek.

Riding the clouds and controlling the qi, rushing like lightning, Ascending to the sky and entering the earth, searching everywhere. Reaching the top of the blue sky and descending to the Yellow Springs, Both places are vast and cannot be found. Suddenly, I heard of a fairy mountain on the sea, The mountain is in the ethereal void. The pavilions are exquisite and clouds rise, Among them, there are graceful fairies. Among them is a person named Taizhen, With snowy skin and floral appearance, she resembles her.

In the west wing of the Golden Palace, knocking on the jade door, Turning to instruct Xiaoyu to report to Shuangcheng. Hearing of the envoy of the Han emperor, Startled in her dream in the Jiuhua tent.

Adjusting her clothes and pushing her pillow, getting up and pacing back and forth, The beaded curtains and silver hooks are slowly opened. The cloud-like hair is half disheveled from her recent sleep, Her floral crown is untidy as she comes down from the hall.

Storytelling

Yao Xiao'an Pang Xueqing Pearl Drop

China & West (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening "Corridor Meeting"

Virtuous and filial woman hurries on a long journey. Carrying a pipa on her back, disguised as a Taoist nun. Weeping at the moon and lamenting at the wind, sighing at her thin fate. Hiding her shame and enduring humiliation to seek her husband. Sad form, lonely shadow. Along the street, transcending and transforming, entering the imperial capital. Coming to the front of the Prime Minister's Mansion, bowing and claiming to be a servant brother. Introduced to the madam, speaking and asking. Where are you from, female Taoist nun? Who is in mourning clothes? Why are you alone in the imperial capital? Madam, my family is from Chenliu County. Because I went to the selection of a good man, there is no news. Asking me whose mourning clothes I am wearing? Three years for my father-in-law, three years for my mother-in-law. Six years of great filial piety on behalf of my husband. I had no choice but to cut and sell my black hair for burial expenses. Crying farewell before the grave, hurrying on a long journey. Hearing that my good man stayed at the Prime Minister's Mansion, I came here specifically to inquire clearly. The madam heard and was shocked. Leaving her seat, she repeatedly said, "I am guilty." Why do you need to inquire so clearly? The person who paints my eyebrows is my husband. Small meeting, sisters changed their names.
